Important News

Zhang Xueliang Telegraphically Denounces Shi Yousan

▲Betraying the Party and the Country is Disloyal▲Indulging Soldiers to Harm the People is Unbenevolent

▲Rebelling Against Superiors is Unrighteous▲Breaking Oaths and Going Back on Words is Untrustworthy

Tianjin Correspondence: The circumstances of Shi Yousan's rebellion have been detailed in previous reports. On the 15th of this month, Shi's army began to advance north from Shunde. The Northeast Army was ordered to retreat, as Zhang Xueliang, considering the internal and external troubles at a critical juncture, did not want to start another civil war and invite contempt. Therefore, he tried to avoid conflict, hoping to prompt Shi's people to awaken. However, Shi insisted on his own way and never looked back. On the 16th, he advanced to Neiqiu, on the 17th to Lincheng, on the 18th to Gaoyi, and on the 19th to Yuanshi. On the 20th, he reached Shijiazhuang, marching straight down as if entering an uninhibited territory. In Shi's mind, he believed that the Northeast Army was not worth fighting, so in five days, he managed to march over 300 miles. In the future, taking Tianjin would be as easy as taking something from a bag. On the evening of occupying Shijiazhuang, he immediately sent a general telegram with his number from Shunde using a wireless spring. The text was 3,000 words long and listed the names of 28 generals. Zhang Xueliang, at this point, could no longer tolerate it and urgently ordered Yu Xuezhong to rush to Baoding to arrange defenses and meet the enemy head-on. The first line of defense was in Zhengding, and the second line of defense was in Wangdu. Zhang's painstaking efforts to maintain peace in North China were now completely hopeless. On the same day (the 23rd), he issued a telegram, which was solemn and righteous. The telegram was already published in the previous report, but there was also a telegram on the (22nd), indicating to the Northeast generals, listing Shi's four major crimes, which was particularly gratifying. The original text is recorded below. Urgent: Commander Yu (Xuezhong) of Baoding, to be transferred to all subordinate brigade commanders; Army Commander Wang (Shuchang) of Tianjin, to be transferred to all subordinate brigade commanders; Garrison Commander Zhang (Xueming) of the Municipal Government; Beiping Garrison Headquarters; Deputy Commander of the Military Police; Commander Fu (ZhanKui) of the Second Cavalry Division; Brigade Commander Miao (Zhuoliu) of the Sixteenth Brigade; Nanyuan Aviation Second Team; Brigade Commander Liu (Yifei) of Zhangjiakou; Brigade Commander Huang (Shiyue) of Renqiu; Brigade Commander Yu (Zhaolin) of Langfang; Shenyang Chief Executive's Office; Northeast Training Committee; Northeast Military Academy; Northeast Aviation Command; Acting Commander Zhang (Zuoxiang); Northeast Military Police Command Commander Chen (Xingya); Guard Commander Liu (Duoquan); Brigade Commander Wang (Yizhe) of the Seventh Brigade; Brigade Commander Zhang (Zuozhou) of Jinzhou; Brigade Commander He (Zhuguo) of Shanhaiguan; Regiment Commander Du of Dalinghe; Zhenshoushi Yu of Hailong; Zhang Zhenshoushi of Taonan; Taonan Reclamation Office; Jilin Deputy Commander-in-Chief's Office, to be transferred to all subordinate divisions and brigade commanders; Zhenshoushi Ding (Chao) of Harbin; Zhenshoushi Shi of Yanji; Zhenshoushi Zhao of Ningguta; Deputy Commander-in-Chief's Office of Qiqihar, to be transferred to all subordinate brigade commanders; Commander Su (Bingwen) of Hailar; Commander Ma of Hailanpao; Deputy Commander-in-Chief's Office of Chengde Prefecture, to be transferred to all subordinate brigade commanders; Deputy Commander Shen (Honglie) of the Qingdao Naval Command, to be transferred to Captain Ling (Xiao), Captain Yuan (Fangqiao), and all captains: Xueliang was previously hospitalized for illness, but fortunately, he has recovered, which is deeply gratifying to all my beloved generals and soldiers, and deeply hated by those who see us as enemies. Now, Shi Yousan, taking advantage of my illness and weakness, led troops to invade northward. His wolfish ambitions and fondness for disorder are well known. First, he betrayed Feng Huanzhang, then Chairman Jiang, and then Yan Baichuan. He disregards faith and righteousness and only seeks profit. Now, he is using his old tricks again on my Northeast. What has my Northeast done to offend Shi Yousan? To sum up his life, he has several evils. The brutality of the Red Bandits is known to everyone. In Xiang, Jiangxi and other provinces, the lessons are clear, but Shi Yousan shared their money, recognized thieves as fathers, and his rebellious actions are obvious and undeniable. Betraying the Party and the country is disloyal. The borders of Hebei and Henan are restless, but Shi's troops stationed there did not quell them but instead colluded with them, mixing soldiers and bandits, tyrannizing the good people, and causing cries of despair in the wilderness and sighs of shared death. Indulging bandits to harm the people is unbenevolent. Shi Yousan came from humble origins and was favored by Feng, who raised him up. As the chief staff officer, his wings grew strong, and he betrayed him. Commander-in-Chief Jiang treated him with sincerity and Yan Baichuan relied on him heavily, but he suddenly abandoned them. My Northeast provided funds and equipment, and his requests were always met. What suspicion or doubt led to his rebellion? His repeated betrayals are shameless and arouse the anger of both gods and men. Rebelling against superiors is unrighteous. Shi Yousan went to Shenyang before, humble and obsequious, crying bitterly to show his sincerity, supporting the central government, swearing to Heaven and Earth. How long has it been? The blood on his mouth has not yet dried, and he has rebelled again. Breaking oaths and going back on words is untrustworthy. Having one of these is unforgivable, let alone all four. He is hastening his own destruction. Now, fortunately, the central government's troops are chasing closely behind, and the Northeast soldiers are attacking head-on. He is like a fish in a cauldron or a beast in a trap. Seizing the flag and breaking through the bamboo will be a matter of time. It is hoped that the generals at the front will encourage their soldiers to bravely fight to be the first, kill the enemy and achieve results, and annihilate these ugly creatures. Wherever they go, they must strictly restrain their troops and not commit the slightest offense. If anyone dares to retreat, disobey military orders, or disturb the people, military law is in place and will not be lenient. The rear troops should intensify training, await orders, and eliminate evil for the country without hesitation. Distinguished service will be rewarded according to the established principles of the country. This is hereby announced in the district, and I cannot help but look forward. In addition, all officers should explain the contents of the telegram to the soldiers in detail to encourage them. Zhang Xueliang, (July 24).

32nd National Affairs Conference of the Executive Yuan

▲Circular order to the whole country to prohibit the occupation of Buddhist temples and monastic property

▲Appointment of He Qigong as member of the Anhui Provincial Government

▲Appointment of Du Xigui as Principal of the Naval Academy

The 32nd National Affairs Conference of the Executive Yuan was held on the 28th. The attendees were Li Shuhua, Ma Fuxiang, Liu Ruiheng, Wang Boqun, and Wang Zhengting. Those present were Zheng Hongnian, Zhang Wohua, Chen Shaokuan, and Chen Yi. The meeting was chaired by Wang Zhengting. Discussion Items: (1) The Ministry of Interior presented a memorandum stating that, regarding the resolutions of the National Assembly, Luo Sang Chu Chen and others proposed safeguarding the civil rights of Han, Mongol, and Tibetan Buddhists as permitted by law. It was ordered to address the matters within the scope of the ministry's jurisdiction. It was found that Item 3 of the original proposal was to issue a circular order from the National Government to the entire country that, in the future, any military police or any organizations, groups, or individuals who occupy Buddhist temples or monastic property will be dealt with according to the law. It was deemed feasible and in accordance with the reason for the presentation to the National Government. The resolution was approved. (2) The Ministry of Interior presented a memorandum stating that, in compliance with orders, it had consulted with the Relief Committee, the Nanjing Municipal Government, and Counselors Chen Rui and Secretary Li Fanguo of the Executive Yuan to prepare for emergency relief for the capital's flood. It was agreed to organize the Capital Flood Emergency Relief Committee, dispatch personnel to investigate the disaster situation, and, before the investigation is completed and the relief efforts are in place, to instruct the Capital Police Department to cooperate with the Nanjing Municipal Government's Social Bureau to distribute relief funds or food, and to plan for the accommodation of the disaster victims. A draft of the Capital Flood Emergency Relief Committee's by-laws was attached, along with detailed figures of the disaster-stricken households and the progress of the relief efforts. The memorandum was presented for review and requested that the by-laws be quickly approved. The resolution approved the by-laws for filing. (3) The Ministry of Industry and the Ministry of Interior jointly presented a memorandum stating that, in compliance with orders, they had drafted regulations for the use of emblems by free professional organizations, and the memorandum was presented for review and compliance. The resolution was passed and will be promulgated by the Executive Yuan. (4) The Board of Directors for the Management of the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Fund presented a memorandum stating that the Central Government had previously decided to use the interest from the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity to subsidize cultural education. The standard for this distribution has now been approved by this conference. The memorandum was presented for review and filing. The resolution was approved for filing and will be forwarded to the National Government. (5) It was resolved to appoint He Qigong as a member of the Anhui Provincial Government. (6) It was resolved to request approval for the resignation of Xia Sunpeng, Principal of the Naval Academy, due to illness, and to appoint Du Xigui to succeed him. (7) It was resolved to approve the resignation of Hu Ruoyu, Director of Mining Affairs, and to appoint Zhou Dawen to succeed him.

Wang Rongbao's Talk Upon Arriving at Shingishu

▲The most severe losses were suffered by our compatriots in Pyongyang

▲The Japanese authorities should bear the responsibility

Minister Wang Rongbao, residing in Japan, arrived at Shingishu at 11:37 AM on July 22nd from Pyongyang. He was greeted by Consul Zhu Fu at the Shingishu Consulate, rested for a few minutes, and then went to meet the Governor of Shingishu. He returned to the consulate at noon, when a reporter arrived at Shingishu from Andong via the river. The reporter immediately visited Wang, who made a statement to the reporter, saying, "I received an order from the Ministry on July 9th to investigate the Korean incident. I departed from Tokyo on the 13th, passing through Busan, Gyeongseong, Incheon, Pyongyang, Zhennampo, and other places. The investigation has lasted more than ten days. Based on what I have learned, Pyongyang has suffered the most severely. The businesses of overseas Chinese can be said to have been completely destroyed. Over 300 large businesses were completely looted, and no goods or furniture were spared. There were originally over 7,000 overseas Chinese in the area. The day of the incident was a Sunday. The local Japanese authorities were all out on holiday, and the more than 200 police officers were also dispersed in various places. By the time the officials learned of the incident, they were unable to stop it. It was not until 3 AM on the sixth day that the police began to wear weapons and go out to guard the area, but it was too late. The damage and looting had already been done. According to the Japanese side, a total of 95 compatriots died tragically in Pyongyang. The place of their burial was inspected by the Minister of Internal Affairs and others from the Provincial Office. There were 95 tombs, each with an altar in front and offerings of incense and flowers. I lingered for a long time before leaving. The Japanese officials said that there was one person in each grave, but they were only temporarily buried. In the future, the Chinese authorities will be able to open the graves and transport the coffins. I think that in the future, when negotiating this case, we must first investigate the exact number of tragic deaths of our compatriots. Opening the graves for verification is probably unavoidable, and the Japanese will probably not refuse. The situation in other places, such as Incheon and Gyeongseong, was lighter, with fewer deaths and injuries.

Photography of the Korean Riot Case (1): The state of Koreans hanging cloths and ribbons on electric poles after a Chinese store in Seoul was destroyed

According to my investigation, there is no way to prove whether Japan had any political role in this Korean riot. However, the Japanese authorities in Pyongyang were negligent in their prevention before the incident and ineffective in their protection during the incident, but they tried their best to provide relief afterwards. It is difficult to absolve them of the responsibility for their negligence. The reason why the Chinese people point fingers at the Japanese for secretly instigating the riot is not without cause. Whenever Koreans cause trouble, they always try to shift the responsibility to the Japanese, saying that they were instigated by the Japanese. Moreover, the Chinese people have always resented Japan, so it is natural for them to be angry with Japan when this incident occurred. However, the Koreans are under Japanese jurisdiction, and no matter how much the Japanese try to quibble, the facts are there, and it is difficult to evade responsibility. As for the damage claimed by the Japanese side, from my point of view, we must first ask whether the overseas Chinese have suffered any losses. If there are indeed losses, Japan must be responsible for compensation. Therefore, I reported to the Ministry based on this idea. It is difficult to obtain an accurate number of losses suffered by the overseas Chinese in Pyongyang without a detailed investigation. Currently, it is estimated that the losses are approximately 2.4 million Japanese yen. Approximately 2,000 overseas Chinese are returning home one after another, but with their families broken and their homes empty, they have no ability to resume business. Returning home is only to handle the aftermath. I visited the injured overseas Chinese in the shelter. There were still 70 injured people in the shelter. When they saw me, they were as if they were seeing their own parents, and they complained one after another. One of them cried and lost his voice because his wife and children had died and his family property had been lost. I comforted him one by one. The shelter is in the Japanese Medical Lecture Hall and has a grass shed that can accommodate about 2,000 to 3,000 people. The living and medical care are acceptable. Various parties have remitted money to provide relief to the overseas Chinese. Approximately 7,000 Japanese yen has been received. On the day the riot occurred, Zhennampo was also in a state of emergency. The local consul was unable to take care of it, which inevitably led to the incident. This must be attributed to the fact that our country did not set up a consulate in Pyongyang. When I came to investigate, I met with Foreign Minister Shidehara, who expressed his extreme apology for the incident in Korea and stated that the government has taken responsibility for suppressing it. The newly appointed Governor-General of Korea, Ura, took office on the 14th, and the Minister of Internal Affairs took office on the 7th. Both have issued orders for strict prevention. I will investigate here (Shingishu) for a day or two and then go to Liaoning to contact the Northeast Political Committee to inquire about the truth of the Wanpaoshan case. Then I will go to Beijing to see Deputy Commander Zhang, and I will go to Beijing via the Jinpu Road in early August." Those who accompanied Mr. Wang included Ren Jiafeng, Consul General in Kobe. When they arrived in Shingishu, overseas Chinese merchants hung up flags to welcome them, and the chief of the Japanese police station also personally led police officers to protect them. (Sent from Andong on the 22nd)

Photography of the Korean Riot Case (2): The state of China Street in Seoul after it was destroyed

The situation of Overseas Chinese Passing Through Andong

▲Over 7,000 people fled back to the country

▲Over 6,000 people have returned home one after another

The reporter arrived in Andong on the evening of July 20th, accompanied by Jin Guanwu and Tian Songsheng, representatives from various groups in Harbin to comfort the overseas Chinese who suffered in the disaster. After arriving in Andong, I wrote a letter to the Yalu River Spring Hotel and visited County Chief Wang Jie Gong and President of the County Chamber of Commerce Sun Langxuan that night, but they were not there because it was late. I visited them again at 8:00 AM on the 21st and found out about the situation of the overseas Chinese in Andong and the relief efforts. The Chamber of Commerce sent personnel to guide me to the overseas Chinese shelter and hospital for investigation. The results are as follows:

▲Number of Overseas Chinese Passing Through Andong: After the Korean riots occurred in Pyongyang and other places, Shingishu, which is separated from Andong by the Yalu River, was initially calm. It was not until the 7th that Koreans suddenly gathered to beat the overseas Chinese. The overseas Chinese were unable to resist and fled to Andong. Fortunately, the river bridge was passable, so it was easy to escape. In the early morning, more than 200 people arrived first, all fleeing alone. With no relatives to turn to, they appointed a representative to lead them to the County Government to appeal to the County Chief. The County Chief then transferred the matter to Zhang Hanwei, Director of the Public Security Bureau, and Sun Langxuan, President of the Chamber of Commerce. It was decided to open the Dan Gui stage as a temporary shelter for the returning overseas Chinese. In the afternoon of the same day, more than 1,000 people arrived again. Since the Dan Gui Garden could not accommodate them, the Xin Ming Theater and the Dongming, Dongping, and Northeast Three Movie Theaters were successively occupied and numbered 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5. As the days went by, more and more refugees returned. In addition to Shingishu, many also came from Pyongyang. All five shelters were suddenly full. The number of men and women reached more than 3,000. Recently, except for those who were injured or had other reasons and did not leave Andong immediately, and 290 people remained in the shelters, the rest were sent back home by local authorities with funds, or transferred to other places to make a living.

▲Detailed Numbers of Those Sheltering in Andong: Some of the overseas Chinese were acquainted with merchants in the streets of Andong and stayed in their homes or hotels, while others were unaware of the official shelters. The Public Security Bureau of the Andong Commercial Port conducted a detailed investigation, and the numbers are as follows: Within the jurisdiction of the First Branch Bureau, the number of men and women staying in hotels was 11, women 146, totaling 857 people; within the jurisdiction of the Second Branch Bureau, the number of men staying in hotels was 95, women 1, totaling 96 people; within the jurisdiction of the Third Branch Bureau, the number of men staying in hotels was 59, women 13, totaling 73 people; within the jurisdiction of the First Branch Bureau, the number of men lodging with merchants was 447, women 137, totaling 584 people; within the jurisdiction of the Second Branch Bureau, the number of men lodging with merchants was 215, women 145, totaling 360 people; within the jurisdiction of the Third Branch Bureau, the number of men lodging with merchants was 197, women 93, totaling 290 people; the number lodging with merchants was 864 men and 370 women, totaling 1,234 people. The number of overseas Chinese who fled from various places was 3,180 men and 1,295 women who fled from Shingishu; 124 men and 50 women who fled from Huancheon; 73 men and 19 women who fled from Pyongyang; 34 men and 7 women who fled from Jeongju; 99 men and 22 women who fled from Shinanju; 6 men and 3 women who fled from Namcheon; 31 men and 6 women who fled from Pihyeon; 10 men and 5 women who fled from Hancheon; 8 men and 2 women who fled from Hwanghae-do; 36 men and 6 women who fled from Bukhadong; 1 man and 3 women who fled from Baengma River; 20 men and 2 women who fled from Incheon; 72 men and 8 women who fled from Bocheon; 10 men who fled from Tasanpo; 3 men who fled from Yeongmae; 2 men who fled from Jogwan; 2 men who fled from Suan; 1 man who fled from Manggyeong; in total, the number of overseas Chinese who arrived in Andong was over 7,000.

Photography of the Korean Riot Case (3): The state of goods being thrown all over the ground in disorder after a Chinese store in Seoul was destroyed

▲Number of Deaths After Arriving in Andong: 24 overseas Chinese who arrived in Andong were seriously injured, and the number of slightly injured was countless. A girl named Shi, aged 12, died on July 8th due to her injuries. Dong Xiaowang Ding Liangshi died on July 9th. Those who were seriously injured were sent to the Andong Charity Hospital for medical treatment. As of July 21st, only Sun Yongnian, his daughter, and four companions were hospitalized. The rest had either been discharged from the hospital and were staying in the shelters or were in a hurry to leave and had painfully set off. The Christian Charity Hospital also sent doctors to the shelters every day to provide care to the injured, so the number of those discharged from the hospital was greatly reduced, which relieved much suffering. According to the Public Security Bureau's investigation, a list of those seriously injured is as follows:

▲ Andong Circles Provide Relief: The Overseas Chinese Refugee Camp, initially established in five locations, was consolidated as many overseas Chinese left. Currently, only 290 people remain in Andong. The other four locations have been merged, and all are now housed in the First Refugee Camp within Dan Gui Yuan. The County Government Public Security Bureau and Chamber of Commerce have each dispatched specialists to establish a refugee camp office within the Yuan, dedicated to handling overseas Chinese affairs. Overseas Chinese receive two meals daily, one at 8 a.m. and another at 4 p.m., consisting of millet porridge and cornbread cakes, accompanied by pickled vegetables. Those wishing to travel elsewhere or return to their hometowns are provided with travel expenses based on their circumstances, and an additional two yuan is given as pocket money per person. Various circles and shops in Andong have voluntarily donated funds, accumulating over ten thousand yuan. Combined with the three thousand yuan raised by various circles in Liaoning, the total amounts to 16,299.20 Andong small silver dollars, 5,278.60 silver dollars, 755 Feng banknotes, and 5 gold banknotes. Over eight thousand yuan has already been spent, but it is feared that this will not be sufficient, and fundraising efforts are still underway.

Mr. Hu Ruoyu's Talk After Returning to Qingdao

▲ Han Fuju Decides to Send Troops to Punish Shi

▲ No Security Problems on the Tianjin-Pukou Railway Line

▲ Military Action Against Shi Will Not Escalate

Qingdao Correspondence: Qingdao Mayor Hu Ruoyu went to Beiping to serve concurrently as Acting Mayor of Beiping Municipality for nearly four months. Recently, Mr. Hu handed over the concurrent post in Beiping, and the merchants and residents of this city eagerly anticipated his return to office to undertake reorganization. He only arrived back in Qingdao on the Jiaoji Railway car at 10:35 last night (the 23rd). Those who welcomed him at the station included members of the Municipal Steering Committee, Jiaoji Railway Chairman Ge Guangting, the Chairman of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and various committee members, totaling about two hundred people. The Public Security Bureau also dispatched security teams to temporarily stand guard near the station. After Mr. Hu got off the train, he briefly interacted with those who welcomed him and then took a car to the official residence to rest. According to Mr. Hu's conversation with a certain dignitary, he originally wanted to return to Qingdao earlier, but his departure was repeatedly delayed due to his slow recovery from illness. Commander Zhang then instructed him to go to Jinan to consult with Chairman Han on all issues in North China, which inevitably led to further delays. The results of his consultation with Chairman Han in Jinan were satisfactory. Han expressed extreme obedience to the Central Government and Commander Zhang. Han said that with the Communist bandits not yet suppressed and diplomatic storms looming, he did not want to see another war break out in North China. Therefore, he had repeatedly offered advice to the Shi army, hoping they would reflect. If Shi remained stubborn, all military actions would follow Commander Zhang's lead. Currently, Shandong's defenses are extremely solid. In the northern part of Shandong, joint defenses have been established with the Northeast Army. There should be no security problems along the Tianjin-Pukou Railway line. Mr. Hu also said that Commander Zhang had indeed recovered from his illness and could be discharged from the hospital after a short period of recuperation. Commander Zhang had already made plans for the steps to be taken in the campaign against the Shi army. The Jin army also expressed great dissatisfaction with Shi's vacillation and inconsistency and decided to unite with the Northeast Army. Commander Yu (Xuezhong) has already departed for the front line, and military affairs at the front are being commanded by him. Henan Commander-in-Chief Liu (Zhi) is also supervising the troops northward. Even if the two armies come into contact, the war will certainly not escalate and can be resolved in the shortest possible time, etc. (July 24th)

Flood Relief News from Jiangsu Province

▲ Thirty-One Counties Report Major Flooding

▲ Relief Meeting to be Held on Thursday

Continuous heavy rain has been pouring down, and reports of major flooding have been pouring in from both sides of the Yangtze River, affecting up to thirty-one counties. The rising water level in the canal north of the Yangtze River, where the dams are in imminent danger, is particularly concerning. After receiving reports from various counties, Civil Affairs Director Hu Pu'an originally intended to personally inspect the disaster areas immediately. However, as the province's relief policy had not yet been fully discussed, he submitted a request to the provincial government for a large special appropriation for disaster relief to assist the severely affected counties in implementing price stabilization measures. He also requested that the provincial Farmers Bank handle the pledge of rice for loans when the new grain comes to market this year. Meanwhile, he dispatched county magistrates to grain-producing counties to urge the reorganization of accumulated grain and to recover misappropriated and embezzled special funds for accumulated grain from previous handlers. Furthermore, he personally drafted this year's relief methods and scheduled a provincial relief meeting for this Thursday (July 30th) to be proposed for discussion. After a decision is made, emergency relief and work relief efforts will immediately be launched. It is also heard that Director Hu, accompanied by the head of the Fifth Section of the department, Lin Wenqin, went to the outskirts of the provincial capital yesterday afternoon for a week-long inspection. According to the department's news, after the disaster relief meeting on Thursday, Mr. Hu will personally go to the disaster areas north of the Yangtze River together with committee member Wang Yiting, etc., for inspection.

Important News Two

Guangji Embankment in Anhui Province Collapses, Causing Disaster

▲ Breach of Over Thirty Zhang, Hundreds of Li Become a Watery Land

▲ Rice Prices in the Provincial Capital Soar, Martial Law Imposed to Maintain Order

Anqing Correspondence: The Guangji Embankment in Anhui Province, due to continuous rising water levels, had been undergoing emergency repairs. However, at 1:00 p.m. on the 26th, the Shangshi Village area at the Qianjiangkou 40 li downstream of Anqing experienced undercurrents and deep erosion of the embankment foot due to excessive flushing by the river tide. Despite rescue efforts, a breach of over thirty zhang occurred. The houses and fields of seventeen bao, spanning over a hundred li within the embankment, instantly turned into a watery land. Countless people and animals were swept away, resulting in a disaster of the magnitude not seen in thirty years. (The embankment had previously collapsed in the 27th year of the reign of Emperor Guangxu during the Qing Dynasty.) After this news spread to the province, the price of rice in Anhui suddenly soared, from ten yuan to twelve yuan per shi. Flour increased from over three yuan to more than five yuan per bag, and there was fierce competition to buy it. Subsequently, officials dispatched military police to stand guard in front of the rice shops to suppress the situation, and order was restored. To provide relief to the disaster victims and maintain public order, Acting Chairman Zhu Xi convened a temporary emergency meeting at the provincial government on the evening of the 26th, attended by party and government committee members, as well as military and police officials. Five measures were decided upon: (1) Designate higher ground outside the city to erect temporary shelters to serve as refugee camps; (2) Assign the Director of the Anqing Public Security Bureau, Li Yue, and the Magistrate of Huaining County, Wang Cuimin, to be responsible for building shelters and providing relief, with the participation of provincial and county party headquarters, various departments of the provincial government, and the Chamber of Commerce; (3) Consult with the General Headquarters and order the Public Security Bureau to temporarily declare martial law; (4) Prohibit disaster victims from entering the city in groups to prevent troublemakers from taking the opportunity to mix in and disrupt public order; (5) Convene the Chamber of Commerce to organize emergency relief and discuss post-disaster arrangements. After the meeting, Fan Xiji, Acting Commander of the Reserve Army Corps, issued an order declaring martial law and appointed Liang Hongen, Acting Division Commander of the 57th Division, as the Martial Law Commander, with Li Yue, Director of the Provincial Public Security Bureau, and Hao Jiajun, Commander of the Provincial Government Guard Regiment, as Deputy Commanders. The 57th Division headquarters was immediately established as the Martial Law Headquarters, and nine articles of martial law were promulgated, stipulating that no pedestrians were allowed to pass through the streets after 10:00 p.m. unless they held a pass issued by the headquarters. All entertainment venues were required to close one hour before the curfew.

At 10:00 a.m. on the 27th, a joint meeting was held at the provincial government, resolving to establish a temporary Guangji Embankment flood relief committee that day. Before the official establishment of the committee, the Huaining County Government and the Provincial Public Security Bureau were requested to continue to be responsible for matters related to the relief of Guangji Embankment. In addition, after the embankment collapsed, the provincial government immediately ordered the Finance Department to quickly allocate 3,000 yuan for emergency relief, which was used by the county government and the Public Security Bureau to set up refugee camps outside the East Gate in Dazhi Lake. Various charitable organizations purchased food and transported it for distribution. The Panbo Management Office dispatched ships to rescue disaster victims. Regarding the rice problem, the provincial government convened representatives of the rice industry to discuss the matter. It ordered the rice purchased in Wu to be quickly transported to the province and one thousand dan of grain from the Wanyi Granary to be milled to maintain the food supply for the people. The County Government Public Security Bureau also issued a proclamation prohibiting rice merchants from raising rice prices and residents from causing trouble due to the disaster. As a result, public order in the provincial capital was extremely peaceful. (July 28th)

Madame Song's Coffin Returns South

▲ Important Figures All Visit the Song Residence to Offer Condolences

▲ Transported to Shanghai by the Hai Chen Warship

Qingdao Correspondence: Madame Song Ziwen passed away in Qingdao on the 23rd. It is learned that after Song Ziwen and Song Zian transported the coffin from Shanghai on the 25th, the encoffining ceremony was held at 12:00 noon on the 26th. Important figures from various institutions and organizations in the city all visited the Song residence to offer condolences. The encoffining ceremony was conducted purely according to Christian rituals, with a church pastor offering prayers. The coffin was transported to Shanghai by the Hai Chen warship today (the 27th). At 8:00 a.m. this morning, the procession departed from the Song residence on Shenyang Road, led by the Public Security Bureau's motorcade. Following were the police alarm car, military band, security team, eighty wreaths sent by various sectors, personnel holding ropes, the hearse, family members, and finally the security team as the rearguard, providing very thorough protection. The hearse was covered with white silk patterns. When passing through various roads, the police blocked the road intersections and prohibited pedestrians from passing. Those who went to hold the ropes included Central Committee member Shao Lizi, Shandong Salt Transport Envoy Yuan Timing, Mayor Hu Ruoyu, Jiaoji Railway Chairman Ge Guangting, Committee member Lu Mengxiong, Jiaohai Customs Supervisor Yuan Siyan, Shandong Provincial Government Representative Zhang Yue, Jianghai Customs Supervisor Tang Haian, Mrs. Han Fuju, members of the Municipal Steering Committee, Chairman of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce Song Yuting and various executive and supervisory committee members, Municipal Government Secretary-General Hu Jiafeng, Director of the Finance Bureau Guo Binghe, Yang Jinsheng of the Social Affairs Bureau, Director of the Port Bureau Li Yucheng, Director of the Public Security Bureau Yu Jinhe, Director of the Public Works Bureau Zhuang Shuhuai, Shandong Tobacco and Alcohol Stamp Tax Bureau Director Xiang Jieren, Northeast Navy Qingdao Office Director Jiang Hongzi, etc., totaling about two hundred people. All walked under the scorching sun, sweating profusely. Around 10:00 a.m., the coffin arrived at the Dagang Wharf. All the personnel bowed three times to the coffin and were carried by porters to the warship. Song Ziwen, Ziliang, and Zian accompanied the coffin to Shanghai. Song Ziwen took the Dalian Maru, which sailed to Shanghai today, back to Shanghai.

Shandong Province Chairman Han Fuju sent a telegram yesterday to express his condolences to Madame Song, which read: "To my brother, Minister Song Ziwen, I have received the telegraph from Qingdao reporting the passing of your esteemed mother, which has shocked me beyond words. My brother, you are always sincere and deeply filial. You have suddenly encountered a great tragedy, which cannot be described in words. I believe that your esteemed mother's teachings were excellent, and she possessed all the blessings. Returning to heaven, she has no regrets in this world. I hope you will restrain your grief, value yourself for the sake of the country, and comfort her spirit. This is my sincere prayer. Respectfully, your younger brother Han Fuju, with seal." (July 27th)

Qin and Han Bricks and Tiles Not Returned to Japanese

▲ Ministry of Education Cables Shandong Education Department to Comply with Jinan Correspondence: The Qin and Han bricks and tiles in the collection of Mr. Gao of Weixian County, Shandong, were recently sold privately at a low price to Mr. Ota, a Japanese national. The Education Department, considering the loss of antiquities as a loss to the nation, invoked the Antiquities Preservation Law and requested the Qingdao Municipal Government and the Jiaoji Railway Bureau to detain the bricks and tiles when they were transported to Qingdao for export. After several negotiations, they were finally transported to Jinan. After being sorted out by the Provincial Library, a brick and tile book exhibition was held on the 21st of this month to arouse public attention and interest in the preservation of antiquities. The exhibition was completed yesterday (the 23rd). However, at this time, the Japanese national Mr. Ota still requested the consul of his country stationed in Jinan to repeatedly demand the bricks and tiles he had purchased from our officials. If they were not returned, he planned to demand the price of the purchase. The Education Department then telegraphed the Ministry to request instructions. The Ministry replied by telegram that the detained antiquities could not be returned and were transferred to the Executive Yuan for instructions. The text of the telegram is recorded on the left: To Director He of the Education Department, Telegram received, the detained antiquities cannot be returned. As for how to deal with the request, it has been transferred to the Executive Yuan for instructions. Please comply after receiving instructions. Ministry of Education, Yang (July 24th)

Local Correspondence

Baoshan

New County Magistrate Zhao Enju Takes Office: Baoshan County Magistrate Qiu Mingjiu was ordered to be dismissed by the Jiangsu Provincial Government, and the vacant position was reassigned to Zhao Enju, the Magistrate of Yangzhou County. It is learned that Mr. Zhao arrived in Baoshan to take office at 10:00 a.m. yesterday. After Magistrate Qiu transferred the county seal, files, and accounts clearly, he left Baoshan by car at around 11:00 a.m. After taking office, the new County Magistrate Zhao immediately announced the appointment of Zhao Shiru as the Chief of the General Affairs Section, You Zhenxia as the Chief of the Finance Section, and Qian Yaonian as the Chief of the Public Security Section. The remaining staff has not been changed.

Songjiang

Communist Bandit Cao Shuming Disturbs the Return of Trial: The County Government dispatched Political Police Chief Dong Futang to the Suzhou High Court on the 28th to comply with the order to bring back Cao Shuming, a Communist bandit, from Fengjing Bi.

Communist Bandit Cao Shuming was brought back to Songjiang for trial by a temporary special court organized by the county.

Anti-Japanese Association Requests Inspection of Japanese Goods: The County Party Headquarters here received a letter from the Shanghai Anti-Japanese Association, stating that a large batch of Japanese goods would be smuggled into Songjiang. It is heard that an Anti-Japanese and Overseas Chinese Protection Association will be held on August 3rd to discuss everything.

Wujiang

Tongli Case of Smuggled Opium Heard Yesterday: It was reported that Xia Xin, the Chief of the Second Public Security Branch in Tongli Town, seized two bags of opium on a boat at Jiangjia Bridge the day before yesterday. It is now heard that Xia seized more than 400 taels of opium, but only more than 100 taels were sent to the County Government. When District Chief Zhou Shihong of the district heard about this, he secretly reported it to County Magistrate Wu. Yesterday, the County Government temporarily detained Branch Chief Xia for investigation.

Rice Prices Rise by More Than One Yuan in Two Days: Continuous rain in the county has submerged the seedlings, and this year's autumn harvest will inevitably be greatly affected. Rice markets everywhere have seen prices soar due to the disappearance of supplies. In various shops in the county, rice prices have suddenly risen by as much as one yuan and two jiao in the past two days. It is heard that if the weather does not clear, prices will continue to rise.

Wuxi

Defendant Detained in Li Case for Trial: The compensation portion of the case of Li Ashou's tragic death was resolved for 4,400 yuan the day before yesterday. Wu Xilin and Zhu Meisen, who had repeatedly failed to appear in court, arrived in court yesterday. Chief Prosecutor Zhou summoned Sun Wuqing, the accountant of Yongyu Silk Factory, and the plaintiffs, Li Bao's wife and Wang Zhao's younger brother, as well as Wang Ciqing, the representative of the support association, and issued warrants for the arrest of the imprisoned criminals Wang Yucheng and Song Ada. The court hearing began, first with Chief Zhou transmitting the warrants to Wang Ciqing, the representative of the support association, and the plaintiffs, Li Bao's wife and Wang Zhao's younger brother. Then, the three defendants, Wu, Zhu, and Sun, were questioned in detail about the 4,400 yuan compensation fee. After three hours, Wu and others admitted that the money had been handed over, but they did not know how it was distributed. As a result, the plaintiffs were dismissed, and the two defendants, Wang and Song, were returned to prison. Zhu Meisen and Sun Wuqing were each released on bail by three stores in a chain of guarantees. Wu Xilin's case was deemed serious, and he was detained pending further interrogation. Wu, upon hearing that he was being detained after paying such a large compensation fee, was sweating profusely and entered the prison in tears.

Appeal for Confiscated National Goods: On the 25th, Lixin Dyeing and Weaving Company entrusted Tongyi Transfer Company to transport fifteen boxes of cloth produced by the factory, a total of 636 bolts, to the Shanghai branch for sale. Unexpectedly, after arriving in Shanghai, they were detained by the Youri Association Inspection Office in Zhabei as Japanese goods. The company argued that the factory's products had previously been granted national goods certificates by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, which were published in the gazette for all provinces and cities to purchase. Furthermore, Japanese goods are only smuggled from Shanghai to the interior, and there is no case of goods being shipped from the interior to Shanghai. The target of the anti-Japanese movement should be to actively promote national goods, so how can it be possible to obstruct the sale of national goods? Yesterday, the company sent a letter to the Chamber of Commerce requesting that it telegraph the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce to notify the Shanghai Anti-Japanese Association to investigate the goods and expedite their return to avoid hindering the sale of national goods and delighting those who hate us.

Li Gong's Corpse Exhumed for Examination Yesterday: The case of the unclear death of Gong, the wife of Li Zhilin, a villager from Li Lane, 142nd Tu, near Yangshu Village in the 16th District (Wan'an City), was initially investigated by county court officials who found no injuries and determined that she had drowned. However, the corpse's father, Gong Gentang, did not trust the findings and petitioned the High Court to send officials to Wuxi to exhume the corpse and conduct a re-examination to seek justice. After receiving the petition, the High Court reviewed the case files and scheduled the exhumation for the 28th. It is learned that at 9:00 a.m. yesterday, Chief Prosecutor Zhou Erkai of the court, accompanied by Prosecutor Du Jiasheng, Secretary Ni, Wu County Coroner Xuan Fang, County Coroner Shen Zuchan, judicial police chief, and more than ten police officers, traveled to Huishan by rickshaw. The coffin was opened by earthworkers, and Coroner Xuan saw that the corpse's flesh had rotted away, making re-examination impossible. He immediately reported to Chief Zhou that only bone steaming and examination could be performed. Chief Zhou opened the court and questioned Gong Gentang about whether he wanted to have the bones steamed and examined. Gong said that his daughter had injuries on both hands, a hole in her right shoulder, two holes in her buttocks, and an injury on her right foot. He hesitated about steaming the bones for examination. Finally, he signed a pledge to steam the bones for examination. Chief Zhou immediately ordered Jiang Zixian, the Tu Chief of Huishan, to purchase all necessary items. After lunch, Chief Zhou returned to the court, leaving Prosecutor Du at the scene for Coroner Xuan to scrape off the rotten flesh from the corpse bones, wash them in water, and number each bone in preparation for bone steaming today (the 29th) to determine whether there were any injuries.

Jiangyin

Case of Public Security Officer Extorting Money Sentenced: At the beginning of Magistrate Peng's assumption of office,

after taking over the case handed over by former Magistrate Li, involving Public Security Bureau officers Xiao Jiaxian and Chen Fusheng, carrying Director Chen Dunshou's handwritten order, extorting a large amount of money from Huang Zuyin, the young master of Huang Wantong, and doctor Jiang Benli for smoking on May 18th, the case was repeatedly interrogated. Because Xiao and Chen were on the run, the case has been silent for a long time. Yesterday afternoon (the 25th), Wu, the trial officer, brought Sun Rongfu, a security bureau officer, to court as a key person involved in the case and sentenced him to three months in prison, to be carried out immediately.

Chief Culprit of Yangku Riot Arrested: During the 17th year, bandits in Yangku and other places in the county rioted, burning, looting, and killing. The bandit leader Zhi Songtao escaped and was wanted with a reward. On the 24th, Bandit Zhi suddenly armed himself and went to Yang, posing as a recruiting officer for the security regiment. He was arrested by the Yangku Protection Regiment's Fourth Public Security Branch and brought to the county for trial on the evening of the 25th.

Changzhou

Important Proposals at the County Government Meeting: The Wuyi County Government convened a county government meeting on the 27th. The following are the important proposals: (1) In response to the order to establish a literature committee, how to determine the number of ex officio and appointed committee members, and where should the committee's address be located? It was decided to forward the matter to the Department of Civil Affairs for review and approval. (2) It was decided that all the city's tower gates, which are about to collapse, should be dismantled and the city gates repaired at the same time. The required funds are planned to be drawn from the construction funds. The Construction Bureau will prepare a budget and submit it to the County Government for forwarding to the Provincial Government and the Departments of Civil Affairs and Construction for review and approval. In addition, the Public Security Bureau will issue a notice to nearby residents to pay attention to danger and ensure safety. (3) The Public Security Bureau proposed to add funding for patrol zones in the city. It was decided that the Property Department would raise funds.

County-Wide Flood, Many Request Reporting of Famine: The entire Wuyi County has suffered from flooding, and all the seedlings of rice and beans have been submerged. There is no hope for the autumn harvest. In recent days, the heads of the first, third, and fifth districts have all reported the disaster situation to the County Government and requested that personnel be dispatched to investigate and survey, hoping to be exempt from land taxes in the future and to raise relief measures.

Zhenjiang

Jiangsu Province Establishes Marine Survey Institute: To improve the fisheries of Jiangsu Province, the Jiangsu Department of Agriculture ordered the Provincial Fisheries Experiment Field to establish a marine survey institute on Chongming Shengshan Island in accordance with the Jiangsu Province Fisheries Facility Plan and implementation steps. All applicable marine observation equipment has also been ordered to be purchased by the field. It is now heard that the department has appointed Zhang Guizun, the technical director of the field, to concurrently serve as the preparation officer for the institute, and Chen Moulang, a technician from the department, to concurrently serve as the biological and salinity testing work.

Nantong

Pingchao Riverbank Rescue Project: The riverbank of Dali Port in the Pingchao District of Nantong has been eroded by tides, causing the embankments to collapse. Representatives of various agencies have decided to expedite the rescue project. On the 27th, the Department of Construction telegraphed the county government, allocating 2,000 yuan from the water conservancy fund, with the remaining funds to be raised locally.

Police Force Tightens Budget: The annual revenue and expenditure in Tongyi County are severely insufficient, and debts have been used to maintain operations for years, resulting in a significant deficit. After deliberation by representatives of various agencies, it was decided to reduce spending within the security budget. Starting from August 1st, the county police force will abolish the special task force, and the Public Security Bureau will also lay off personnel. All district defense corps will uniformly conscript civilians, and the necessary severance pay will be funded by the county government.

Eastern Township Flood Relief Measures: Nantong has been hit by continuous rain, with the eastern eight districts being the most severely affected. The accumulated water in the fields is seven to eight feet deep and has not receded. The County Government Construction Bureau has sent officials to handle the relief efforts, first considering opening dams downstream and adding culverts to discharge water into the sea. At the same time, they will dredge the silted-up Yao Wang and other sluices to facilitate drainage. For the affected households, each district will raise funds for relief on its own.

Yangzhou

Firefight Between Police and Bandits at Huo Bridge: Wang Qingjiang, the captain of the Taixian County Police Force, led his team to Huo Bridge in Jiangdu County to capture bandits. They arrived in Xianzhen early on the 27th and specially obtained permission from the local merchant corps to send a team to assist. However, upon arriving at Huo Bridge, the bandits opened fire, resulting in casualties on both sides. The county has received a report from the captain regarding the situation and has requested that a team be dispatched to assist in the suppression. A telegram has already been sent to the Taixian County Government to send additional police forces.

Director Li Sends Representative to Yangzhou: Li Mingzhong, the Pacification Director of Henan, Anhui, Hubei, and Suiyuan, has sent Liu Ganchen, the director of the Military Law Department, as his representative to Yangzhou to meet with Director Zhang Zhijiang of Jiangsu, to present everything and discuss pacification matters.

Five Counties Telegraph Request to Retain Liang's Troops: Party and government agencies and civil groups from Siyang, Suqian, Suining, Huaiyin, and Shuyang counties have jointly telegraphed to Zhang Zhijiang, the Pacification Director, stating that with the rise of the “green gauze tents” and the rampant banditry, they have heard news that the 25th Route Army may be transferred elsewhere. They request that the troops not be transferred in order to maintain local security in their respective counties. It is unknown what instructions the Director's office will issue.

Pinghu

Main Culprit in the Zhouwei Town Robbery Arrested: Zhouwei Town in the county was previously robbed twice by bandits. Subsequently, military and police agencies arrested Jiang Lairong, a suspect, as the main culprit and detained him at the Xincang Public Security Bureau. Since the mutiny of the 16th Regiment stationed in Xincang, Jiang was released by the mutineers and used as a guide. It was recently learned that the Zhouwei robbery was committed by Jin Heshang and Jin Xiaodi, bandits under the command of Liu Dexing (who has already been executed). It was also learned that Jiang Lairong had been hiding at home recently. Therefore, Jiang was arrested and ordered to lead the neighborhood officials to Wangwan to investigate. As a result, the two Jins were arrested. They were escorted to the township office and sent to the rural clearing sub-bureau for investigation.

Hangzhou

Hangzhou Tap Water Fully Tested: The Hangzhou Tap Water Planning Committee has completed most of the work on the sedimentation tank, clear water tank, and Ziyang Mountain regulating reservoir outside Qingtai Gate, as well as the installation of water pipes. A full test was conducted starting yesterday (the 28th) to verify the water supply situation of the installed water pipes in various locations. Engineer Chen from the committee personally inspected each section and dispatched personnel to repair any issues. The results were quite good, and it is expected that water supply can be implemented starting August 1st to meet the needs of citizens.

While traveling to Wushan, his second son fell and was unable to continue. ... Afterwards, neighbors reported to the local Public Security Bureau for investigation. It is known that the new County Magistrate Wu arrived in the county with more than ten staff members from various departments around 6 PM on the 25th and took office on the morning of the 27th.

Continued Report on the Yuyao Fast Boat Robbery: Regarding the robbery of the fast boat traveling from Shangyu City to Houqingmen in Yuyao around 10 AM on the 22nd in Anwan, where about 1,000 silver dollars were stolen, according to subsequent information, there are slight discrepancies with the previous report. This time, the Heng brand sauce garden suffered a loss of over a hundred yuan, and the Xiankang Farm lost four hundred yuan and one thousand dimes. The other two hundred yuan belonged to the Yuanshun Oil Company and the Xiejiabao Dayou Heng Native Products Store. The reason is that during the robbery, the funds from Xiankang Farm were placed in a separate burlap sack, which was placed in a remote corner of the cabin and covered by a passenger's suitcase, so it was not seen by the bandits. When the bandits threatened and questioned the boat owner Hong Toumao and the hired worker Shui Jin, Shui Jin, in a panic, mistakenly handed over a burlap sack containing one hundred yuan each from the Dayou Heng and Yuanshun companies, as well as scattered silver dollars from various merchants, thus escaping danger. The total loss, including a gold watch and chain belonging to a passenger, is estimated at over four hundred yuan.

Hefei

Record of the Sensational Bone-Robbing Case in the County: The bone-robbing case that has attracted attention throughout the county was publicly tried by Section Chief Yu at the county government on the 20th. The audience from all walks of life was extremely crowded. The first to be interrogated was the sorcerer Hu Youzhi, who claimed to be 107 years old, born in the fifth year of the Daoguang reign. He served as a mid-level military officer in the former Qing Dynasty. Later, he crossed the East Sea and was taught the art of immortality and healing by a celestial being. He returned to China and treated many people in Beijing, Tianjin, Shanghai, Wuhan, Wuhu, and Chaohu. He repeatedly denied any involvement in the bone-robbing case. Then, the son-in-law of Dan Guo, Zu Muheng, testified that the sorcerer's magic was profound and he had many disciples in major ports such as Beijing, Tianjin, Shanghai, and Wuhan. He claimed to be unaware of the details of the bone-robbing, kidney-cutting, and breast-cutting. The sorcerer was temporarily detained, and Zu and Dan Guo were placed under guard. At the same time, Section Chief Jin of the Public Security Bureau interrogated Dan Shuzhang, the second daughter of Dan Guo, at the Hong residence. She testified that her mother had invited the old Daoist to treat her when she was young, so she knew him. She was allowed to reside there for this reason. As for the letter from Cai, a woman from Chaoxian County, saying that she was suffering in front of her master's bed, she had been classmates with her at the Chaoxian Christian Girls' School, and her words referred to being disciplined by the principal. There was no concrete evidence. However, the 46th Division, considering the seriousness of the case, took the sorcerer to the military court that night for a secret interrogation to clarify the truth. At 2 PM, various public organizations held a joint meeting at the Chamber of Commerce. Someone reported that they had inquired with a maid of the Dan family, who said that the old Daoist had many female disciples who had been accepted, called the Eight Trigram Furnace. Those who attained enlightenment would be able to escape disaster in the years of the Rooster and Monkey, when the heavens and earth would be turned upside down. However, he had recently hired craftsmen to make many axes and saws, and it was not known what they were for. Those present at the meeting believed that the case had many suspicious points and must be related to the bone-robbing case. They decided to elect representatives such as Li Taoran and Yang Licuo to petition the division headquarters and county government to reinvestigate the case to reassure the public.

Educational News

Important News

Ministry of Education Prohibits Private Universities from Enrolling Students in Specialized Accelerated Courses

The Ministry of Education issued a circular to education departments and bureaus in various provinces and cities, instructing all private universities and colleges to stop enrolling students in specialized accelerated courses starting this year. The circular stated that the most urgent task for universities is to enrich their content and improve their standards. However, in recent years, private universities and colleges have often indiscriminately established specialized accelerated courses to attract students, which is prone to abuses. Starting this year, all schools should stop enrolling students in the aforementioned affiliated courses to prevent abuse. If necessary, they may establish specialized courses in accordance with Chapter 5 of the University Regulations, but they must first submit them to the Ministry for approval before enrolling students. In addition to distributing this to various departments, the "Department" and "Bureau" are hereby ordered to immediately forward it to all registered private universities and colleges and those with registered school boards for compliance. This order.

Gentry of Chongming County Continue to Run Chongming Middle School

Chongming County Middle School has a history of sixteen years since its founding. Since the departure of Principal Wang Shaoji, the department ordered the cessation of enrollment and the gradual closure of the school. The local elders were very indignant. Now, dozens of people, including Zhang Dingzhi and Su Renquan, have jointly submitted a petition to the department and county, stating that the county school is necessary for the local area and that there is a dedicated land tax to maintain it. They requested that enrollment continue, and Jin Fengming also sent a special letter to the director of the department, enumerating the reasons, saying that the retention or departure of the principal affects the overall situation of the school.

The motion was passed as proposed. The finance and education departments also jointly proposed to change the originally scheduled land tax donation rate of two dimes in He County to an additional one dime and five fen per tael and dan of silver and rice, so that the county's education funds could be increased. The motion was passed.

Local News

Organization of the Chinese Veterinary Education Promotion Association

▲ Establishment of a Veterinary Specialized Course

Zou Bingwen, director of the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau, Cai Wuji, and veterinary expert Wang Zhaoqi, recognizing the importance of veterinary education, organized the Chinese Veterinary Education Promotion Association. Zou Bingwen, Cai Wuji, Wang Zhaoqi, Xiang Songmao, Shen Jiuru, Ye Hancheng, Jiang Wenyu, Huang Renzhi, Yang Weiyu, Pan Yangyao, and others were publicly elected as members. A veterinary specialized course was established at the China Vocational Education Society, enrolling forty students and ten medical students (both male and female can start recruiting). The association's regulations are excerpted as follows: (1) The purpose of this association is to promote the development of veterinary education and implement veterinary education. (2) This association is composed of veterinary experts, enthusiastic comrades in veterinary undertakings, and leaders of administrative agencies related to veterinary undertakings. (3) The association has a temporary committee of fifteen members, from which three standing committee members are publicly elected to preside over daily affairs. (4) The association's business includes: 1. Implementing veterinary education and establishing specialized schools; 2. Promoting and publicizing veterinary education; 3. Researching the curriculum and facilities of veterinary education; 4. Introducing the supply and demand of veterinary talents; 5. Other undertakings related to veterinary education. (5) The association holds a regular meeting on the first Wednesday and Friday of each month at 4 PM. Temporary meetings may be held in case of special important matters. (6) Members of the association pay annual dues of two yuan, payable in mid-July each year. (7) If there are any matters not covered in the association's regulations, they may be amended at any time.

Translation of Famous Works

Recently, Shi Youzhong, Wang Shixian, and several other alumni of Yenching University and Shanghai University, in view of the recent upsurge in domestic academic activities and the new spirit of the Chinese people in praising Western masterpieces, invited comrades to organize a translation group in Shanghai, specializing in introducing the works of authoritative authors in Europe and the United States to meet the needs of the Chinese people. The group has mostly completed the translation of two books: one is Montague's Ways of Knowing, which is the only systematic famous work on philosophical methodology in the last ten years, aiming to separate methodology from the confusion of cosmology and give it a clear outline. The content is divided into two parts and a dialogue, with a total of more than 200,000 words. The other is Dickinson's International Anarchy. People of the Dickinson family all know that he is the authoritative person in modern international studies. The content of this book describes the historical materials that caused the European War in 1914 and reveals the inside story of the secret diplomacy of various countries before the war. Dickinson's views are fair, and it is a must-read for those who study modern world diplomatic history. This book also has more than 200,000 words.

Charity Match Before Trip to Java: Sino-Portuguese Team Decisively Defeats Navy

—Result: Seven to One—

Hong Kong Dispatch, July 20th. The Nanyang Brothers Tobacco Company is raising funds to provide relief for the flooding in the Three Rivers region. They invited the South China Athletic Association's touring football team to play a charity football match against the Hong Kong Navy football team. The proceeds from the ticket sales will be used for disaster relief. Yesterday afternoon at 5:00 PM, the two teams competed at the Sister Islands Stadium. A large crowd attended. The South China team won decisively with a score of seven to one. The starting lineups for both teams were as follows:

▲South China Team Lineup

Zhou Xiyan, Li Ning, Feng Yunyou, Chen Zhenhe, Lin Yuying, Li Guozhao

Chen Guanghui, Sun Jinshun, Da Gao Shannu, Chen Jiaqiu, Xiao Gao Shannu

▲British Navy Team Lineup

Luo Weizhi, Nu Bili, Jia Da, Ge Da Li, Bao Liedun, Wei Luson

Ba Lanchi, Luo Chen, Wei Yi, Shan Te, Yun Chen

The Navy's lineup today was not significantly different from their lineup in the previous week's game against the Guangdong Navy. The Sino-Portuguese South China touring team fielded their best players. The Navy conceded four goals in the first half and one goal to three in the second half. The result was a decisive defeat of seven to one. Da Gao Shannu was the standout player of the day. Less than five minutes into the game, he capitalized on a clever cross from Sun Jinshun to score the first goal. Five minutes later, Chen Jiaqiu scored again. After twenty minutes of intense play, Chen scored another goal. After a kickoff from midfield, Chen Guangyao seized an opportunity to pass into the center, and Gao scored his fourth goal within a minute. After the break, Sun Jinshun received the ball in midfield and dribbled to a good position before passing it to Da Gao Shannu. Gao advanced on a one-on-one, and Luo Weizhi rushed out of the goal, but Gao easily dribbled past him and gently kicked the ball into the net. Soon after, Chen Guangyao received the ball and passed it to Sun Jinshun. Sun crossed, and Gao Shannu scored the sixth goal. The seventh goal was scored by Sun Jinshun, making it seven to zero. Unexpectedly, the Navy's left-back Luo Chen managed to break the shutout in the final ten minutes. As a result, the South China team won by a score of seven to one. After the match, Luo Xushi presented the awards: a silver cup to each team and a fountain pen to each player. He praised all the players for their enthusiasm for charity and gave three cheers before the crowd dispersed.

Special Article

A New Aspect of Chinese Education

—Central Political School (3) Ye Xing

Expenses such as laundry and haircuts are also provided by the school. Unless there are special circumstances and with the approval of the team leader, students are not allowed to ask for leave to go out. The atmosphere of seeking knowledge at the school is unusually strong. There are no absences from classes, and there are no disciplinary problems. Moreover, the seats in the library and self-study rooms are always full. Students are always respectful to their teachers, whether on or off campus, raising their right hand to their hat brim in a salute. When a teacher enters the classroom, a student will call out the command "Attention!" and the entire class will stand up straight. Therefore, new instructors, especially those who have taught at universities nearby, are often surprised when they step into the classroom. Visitors all say that the school has a culture of respecting teachers. The examinations for students are extremely strict. If cheating or any other misconduct is discovered during an exam, the student is immediately expelled without leniency. Moreover, if a student fails several subjects in the final exams, they are also immediately expelled. Therefore, of the current third-year students, who numbered more than 413 when they first enrolled, only over 270 remain after three years. From this, one can see the strictness of the school. When the school was first established, it borrowed a portion of the old Southeast University site. Later, it moved to the old Jiangsu College of Law and Politics site in Hongzhilang. Some money was saved from the annual operating expenses and used to build four or five new-style buildings, but it is still not enough. The school has other plans, intending to find another site and use the current site to establish an affiliated senior high school or vocational school. However, this is still in the planning stages. The school's operating expenses are extremely low. With nearly 500 students, over 80 professors and lecturers, plus staff from the military training department, translation department, and library, the monthly expenditure is only over 27,000 yuan. Therefore, Mr. Zhang Boling, the president of Nankai University, said that this school is even more economical than private universities. However, the school is not at all stingy when it comes to purchasing books and equipment. For example, when the school implemented group studies this year, it specifically allocated 20,000 yuan for purchasing books and equipment. The annual expenditure on books and equipment accounts for 15% of the annual operating expenses, amounting to over 30,000 yuan. Therefore, although the library's collection cannot be considered large compared to libraries with collections in all disciplines, it is a relatively well-equipped specialized library. After visiting China, Harvard University Professor Holcomb wrote a book called "The Chinese Revolution," in which he described the library as an "Excellent Library of Political Science," which is a very accurate assessment.

Because the school aims to cultivate talents with practical specialized knowledge and skills, it emphasizes both theory and practice. Since it is located in the capital, there are many opportunities for internships. For example, the Central Party Headquarters, the Nanjing Municipal Government, and other ministries and commissions often recruit students from the school to help when they need to conduct statistics. In this way, the students can gain a lot of practical experience. For the rural administration group's internship, the school not only established a farm but also assigned students to various farms during the summer vacation for practical experience. The school also specifically designated one semester, the first semester of the fourth year, as the internship period. The National Government assigns each student to various counties and cities for internships, so that they have adequate practical experience in preparation for their future work assignments, so that they will not be at a loss and overwhelmed when the time comes. After a semester of internship, the students are recalled to the school for another semester of study. They are required to discuss the difficulties and problems they encountered during their internships and write a thesis. Only after the thesis has been reviewed and approved are they allowed to graduate. This is also a special feature of the school's educational implementation. Because the school has limited funds and is extremely economical in its spending, it adopts a cautious and steady approach to future development. It first focuses on enriching the internal curriculum and facilities and then seeks to expand on a comparable scale. Once the school site issue is resolved, it will not be difficult to establish specialized classes such as statistics and accounting. The enrollment quota will be slightly increased to 300 students in the second half of the year, and an education department will be added. At the same time, two groups will be established: educational administration and rural education. The school is actively increasing its reference materials and continuing to hire professors. If this continues, the school will definitely reach a considerable scale in five years. This school is not only an important educational institution for cultivating practical political talents but also the best way out for poor and ambitious young people. No wonder it has attracted the attention of the entire country. (End)
