Local News

The French Concession Agreement Was Signed in Nanjing Yesterday

▲Contents: Fourteen Articles and Three Annexes

Nanjing Dispatch: The Shanghai French Concession Agreement, consisting of fourteen articles, was signed yesterday by representatives Lai Gede and the Director of the European and American Affairs Department on the Chinese side. The agreement comprises fourteen articles and three annexes. The Chinese side is very understanding of the French side's concerns regarding this matter. The Chinese courts' regulations concerning French advisors and lawyers are also stipulated in the annexes. The deadline for the handover of the prison was also agreed upon amicably by both parties. It is anticipated that the fourteen articles and the annexes will be approved by both governments. The date of publication has not yet been determined, but it is expected that the fourteen articles will be published in advance soon.

Another report states that the French Consul General in Shanghai, Gan Gelin, went to Nanjing by night train last night. It is said that he was instructed by his government to begin negotiations with Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting regarding the National Government's recovery of the French Concession.

Good News for National Flood Relief

▲Organization of the Shanghai Relief Committee for Provincial Flood Relief

Continuous heavy rains have persisted for almost two weeks, and the flood situation in various provinces is critical. Last night, Chairman Xu Shiying and committee members Wang Yiting and Li Jin of the Relief Committee convened a meeting at Jue Lin, inviting philanthropists from all walks of life in Shanghai to discuss emergency flood relief measures. More than thirty people attended, including Lin Kanghou, Xie Hengchuang, Yu Qiaqing, Xiang Maosong, Wen Lanting, and Hong Yanbin. It was decided on the spot to organize the Shanghai Relief Committee for Provincial Flood Relief. All attendees became members of the preparatory committee, and a general assembly will be established within days. Chairman Xu went to Nanjing that evening to prepare for the Relief Committee's emergency relief work and will return to Shanghai to preside over the general assembly.

Various Shipping Companies Received Yangtze River Flood Alerts Yesterday

▲Warehouse Piers in Various Ports Flooded

▲Shipping Companies Rushing to Reinforce Day and Night

▲Cargo Transport Disrupted in Central Anhui

▲Warehouses Submerged in Water Yesterday, shipping companies along the Yangtze River in this city received urgent telegrams from Hankou stating that continuous heavy rains in Hankou have caused a sudden rise in the river level. Today, the water has overflowed onto the banks, reaching within two feet of the highest warehouses. The lower warehouses are already flooded, and the damage to cargo is unprecedented. The water level is still rising. Warehouses have hired large numbers of workers to move cargo and reinforce defenses.

▲Urging Customers to Pick Up Goods The telegram to Shanghai was followed by another urgent telegram, stating that the Yangtze River level had reached 49 feet 5 inches, an unprecedented record high for the Yangtze River. The entire area from the First Pier is submerged. Shipping companies are working day and night to move cargo, but there is a backlog of stored goods and insufficient warehouse space. If the situation continues, the damage from the water will increase, making it more difficult to move cargo, and the losses will be even greater. It is requested that Shanghai Yangtze River shipping companies jointly notify customers with goods stored in Hankou to pick up their goods within a limited time, otherwise the shipping companies will not be responsible.

▲Customers Responsible for Water Damage After receiving this warning yesterday, shipping companies notified customers and telegraphed their branches and warehouse managers in Zhenjiang, Nanjing, Wuhu, Datong, Anqing, Wuxue, Jiujiang, and other ports along the Yangtze River to inform their customers that severe flooding has occurred in various ports along the Yangtze River. Most warehouses are submerged in water. This is a natural disaster that cannot be resisted by human effort. The companies are not responsible for any damage to goods caused by water. The cost of moving and transferring goods will be borne by the cargo owners.

▲Yangtze River Cargo Transport Disrupted The flooding is also very severe in southern and northern Anhui. All embanked fields are submerged. Recently, the import and export of goods to and from ports such as Wuhu, Datong, and Anqing have been disrupted by the flooding. Customers transporting goods to the interior of Anhui have stopped transporting due to disrupted transportation. The amount of cargo transported up and down the river by the Six Companies' Yangtze River steamers at Wuhu and Anqing has been greatly reduced.

All Small Steamers in Shanghai Suspended

▲Severe Flooding in Jiangsu; Severe Drought in Eastern Zhejiang

Severe flooding has struck Jiangsu Province, completely disrupting inland waterway traffic and inundating vast swathes of farmland. Meanwhile, in Ningbo, just hundreds of miles away, an unusually severe drought has persisted for over a month, threatening to cause a famine. The latest news received yesterday is detailed below.

▲Small Steamers to Suzhou and Hangzhou Also Suspended From the 6th and 7th days of this month until now, continuous heavy rain has been falling. Over thirty routes of small steamers on the inland waterways of Jiangsu Province have been completely suspended. From the Shanghai side, only two lines, the Shanghai-Suzhou and Shanghai-Hangzhou lines, were barely able to operate. However, since the continued heavy rains began on the 25th, the water level in the interior has risen even further. In Suzhou, the river water has submerged the banks, reaching over a foot deep, turning the waterways into a vast expanse of water. Yesterday, shipping companies in Shanghai suspended the Suzhou line. Initially, the Hangzhou line was still considered passable, but now the water level is so high that it has reached the level of the bridge arches. Even small civilian boats cannot pass, so it has also been suspended.

▲Shanghai-Jiaozhou Line Partially Suspended Of all the small steamers on the inland waterways of Shanghai, only the Shanghai-Jiaozhou line is still barely operating. However, yesterday, the China Merchants Bureau received reports that while the water level in Zhujiajiao was not too high, in Qingpu, the rivers have flooded the farmland, making it impossible to distinguish the waterways from the land. According to the Bureau's proposal, the Shanghai-Jiaozhou line should be suspended. However, due to the requests of local merchants and residents to prevent the disruption of transportation, the Bureau has instructed the captain of the Shanghai-Jiaozhou steamer that, upon arriving at Qingpu, the driver should not drive the boat but only allow it to float with the current to avoid damaging the embankments. Therefore, while this route is still operating, it is effectively in a state of partial suspension.

▲Severe Drought in Eastern Zhejiang Yesterday, a friend from Ningbo reported that Ningbo has not received a single drop of rain since the beginning of summer, which has been almost a month. The region is facing a severe drought. Zhenhai, Fenghua, and other places have also been without rain for over a month. Rivers are drying up, and people are finding it difficult to find drinking water. In Zhenhai, the early rice crop is almost ripe and ready for harvest, but many plants have already withered and died due to the drought. The late rice crop is also about to be planted, but it will likely wither and die due to the drought. If it does not rain for another week, there will be no hope for the late rice crop, and the region is very concerned about becoming a drought-stricken area.

▲Suppress Bandits, Punish Traitors, Oppose Japan, Aid Overseas Chinese

Various trade associations, labor unions, and other civil groups in this city, recognizing the dual threat of internal strife and foreign aggression, have jointly launched a citizens' assembly to suppress bandits, punish traitors, oppose Japan, and aid overseas Chinese in order to galvanize the nation towards a common goal. Recognizing that the nation is facing both internal strife and foreign aggression, and that the people of the entire country urgently need to suppress the Red bandits, punish Shi Yousan, aid overseas Chinese, and resolutely carry out an economic boycott against Japan, the association plans to convene a city-wide citizens' assembly to serve as a backing for the government. This City Begins Fundraising for a Grain Storage Fund

▲Target Amount: One Million Yuan

The Shanghai Food Committee, recognizing that the food supply for the citizens of this city is often in a precarious and unstable state, has noted that while famine should be reported immediately, even continuous rain can cause rice prices in this city to rise. After careful investigation, the committee found that this is because the city has a population of over three million, the majority of whom are of modest means and rely on other ports for their rice supply. Even slight shortages or difficulties in transporting goods can cause rice prices to rise sharply, making it impossible for the poor to have a stable livelihood. Even in the event of a famine, attempts to regulate the market and prevent food shortages are hampered by a lack of funds, making it impossible to take effective action, increasing losses during temporary interventions. Therefore, the committee proposed raising a grain storage fund in advance, so that funds would be available and all disaster preparedness measures could be implemented in due course. The committee submitted a request to the Social Bureau, which in turn submitted it to the Municipal Government for approval. The committee then appointed members and established the Shanghai Grain Storage Fund Raising Committee in October of last year, deciding to raise one million yuan by forming teams to raise money together. It has been heard that the recent heavy rains have caused disasters, making the need to store grain even more urgent. Therefore, the committee has now begun forming teams to raise funds.

▲Selection of Team Leaders The team leaders are Wang Yiting, Yu Qiaqing, Qian Xinzhi, Wang Xiaolai, Qin Runqing, Hu Jiameng, Wu Zhenxiu, Xu Jiqing, Gu Xinyi, Yuan Ludeng, Yao Zirang, Liu Hongsheng, Shen Lianfang, Yao Mulian, Wang Yansong, Ye Huijun, Lin Kanghou, Zhu Zixiang, Lu Wenshao, Lao Jingxiu, Zhu Wenqi, Sun Baorong, Pan Gongzhan, Tang Naikang, Zhu Hao, Gu Shiguang, Chen Yafu, Chen Tianxi, Pan Hongding, Tang Chengzong, Zhu Zonglu, Yan Enzuo, and Hong Lanxiang. The team leaders will introduce local enthusiasts to serve as team members in order to achieve the fundraising goal as soon as possible. It has been heard that Xu Shengchan, Zhu Yinjiang, Lu Bohong, Xu Xinliu, Li Fusheng, Chen Guangfu, Feng Bingnan, Rong Zongjing, Cai Zengji, Pei Yunqing, Tang Shoumin, and Cheng Zhusun have also been newly appointed as team leaders.

▲Honors for Donations The Municipal Social Bureau believes that the government should encourage and reward people from all walks of life who are enthusiastic about donating. It has drafted fundraising measures, which have been submitted to the Municipal Government for approval and implementation. Article 4 states that donors, whether individuals or organizations, will be rewarded according to the "Regulations on Commending Donations for Relief Efforts" promulgated by the National Government, depending on the amount of their donations. (1) Donors of 5,000 yuan or more will have their names submitted by the committee to the mayor, who will then submit them to the National Government for an award plaque. (2) Donors of 1,000 yuan or more but less than 5,000 yuan will have their names submitted by the committee to the mayor for an award plaque. (3) Donors of 500 yuan or more but less than 1,000 yuan will have their names submitted by the committee to the Municipal Social Bureau for an award plaque. Those who donate more than five times the amount listed in Article 4 will also be eligible for a comparable award.

▲Fundraising Notice The committee issued a fundraising notice yesterday, which stated that "It has been taught in the classics that three years of farming must have one year of food storage, and nine years of farming must have three years of food storage. Therefore, even in the event of famine or flood, the people will not starve. Zhou officials also established 'residual grain officers' to provide relief to the people with the grain reserves of villages and neighborhoods, and to prepare for famine with the grain reserves of counties and capitals. That is how careful they were about storing grain. Our late Premier Sun Yat-sen also stated that only with the construction of charitable granaries and the storage of three years of surplus grain can the food problem of the people be truly resolved. Abundance and scarcity are not determined by human power, and the food problem of the people is the core of the people's livelihood. Therefore, grain storage is highly valued in both ancient and modern times. This city has a population of over three million and is located at a strategic point on land and sea routes, so there is no fear of lacking food. However, because the city does not produce rice, the population is large, and most people are of modest means, the effects of rice shortages and high prices are quickly felt. In the event of famine, regulating the food supply temporarily can only provide limited relief. As the saying goes, 'Only with preparation can there be no fear.' After the food shortages of 1929 and 1930, people in society have become aware that disaster preparedness efforts cannot be delayed. Therefore, the government has established this committee, bringing together local gentry and merchants, to plan for the construction of grain storage facilities and to raise a fund of one million yuan. Moreover, the recent continuous rains have caused disasters, and the fields in the rice-producing areas throughout the country have been flooded, dashing hopes for the autumn harvest. The panic to come is not yet over. The regulation and distribution of the food supply should be planned in advance so that we are not digging a well only when we are thirsty. The committee has decided to begin forming teams to solicit donations immediately. There are many enthusiastic philanthropists in Shanghai who are happy to do good. As this matter concerns the livelihood of all citizens, we urge you to donate generously and support the creation of a grain storage foundation to prevent food shortages. We respectfully pray for the blessing of the poor. Sincerely, Wang Yiting, Yu Qiaqing, Qian Xinzhi, Wang Xiaolai, Qin Runqing, Hu Mengjia, Wu Zhenxiu, Xu Jiqing, Gu Xinyi, Yuan Ludeng, Yao Zirang, Liu Hongsheng, Shen Lianfang, Yao Muyun, Wang Yansong, Ye Huijun, Lin Kanghou, Zhu Zixiang, Lu Wenshao, Lao Jingxiu, Zhu Wenqi, Sun Baorong, Pan Gongzhan, Tang Naikang, Zhu Hao, Gu Shiguang, Chen Yafu, Chen Tianxi, Pan Hongding, Tang Chengzong, Zhu Zonglu, Yan Enzuo, and Hong Lanxiang, team leaders of the Shanghai Grain Storage Fund Raising Committee. Association address: Social Bureau, Zhonghua Road, Nanshi."

Ongoing News of Resisting Japanese Goods

▲ Temporary General Meeting of the Chamber of Commerce

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, since its temporary members' meeting on the 24th, has resolved to automatically sever economic ties with Japan, participate in the anti-Japanese movement, and organize registration of Japanese goods and two committees for inspection and research. It is now actively proceeding according to the resolutions. Details are as follows:

▲ Busy Registering Japanese Goods. After the chamber handled the registration of Japanese goods for member stores affiliated with industry guilds, those coming to register at the chamber have been very busy in recent days. More than 5,000 registration forms have been issued, all limited to being filled out and submitted to the chamber before August 6th, so that they can be compiled and forwarded to the Anti-Japanese Association for handling in accordance with regulations. During the registration period, all Japanese goods should be stopped from being declared, transported, and sold.

▲ Circular to Various Industries with Methods. The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce yesterday sent a circular to all members, requesting various industries to recommend research committee members and inspection committee members for resisting Japanese goods. The circular stated: (1) Respectfully informing you, regarding the matter of economic severance with Japan, the chamber held a temporary members' meeting on the 24th of this month to discuss methods. According to the proposal of the Knitting Industry Guild, the domestic double-strand thread is insufficient for application. Please properly discuss and formulate good solutions. It was proposed to the general meeting for detailed discussion and resolution that there should be specific classified and phased methods for resisting Japanese goods. At the same time, it was resolved that the organizational law of this research committee for resisting Japanese goods should be drafted by the standing committee, and the members should be recommended by various industries. Correspondingly, the case is recorded and the letter is delivered. Immediately request your guild to recommend one member within three days of receiving this letter and report to this chamber for organization and establishment without delaying the progress, as it is extremely important. (2) Respectfully informing you, regarding the matter of economic severance with Japan, the chamber held a temporary members' meeting on the 24th of this month to discuss methods. According to the proposal of the Seafood and Grocery Guild, inspection is the most difficult part of resisting Japanese goods. Each industry should recommend an expert in identifying goods to organize a review committee to avoid disputes. It was resolved that representatives should be nominated by each industry and reported to this chamber to jointly organize a commercial inspection committee for Japanese goods. Correspondingly, the case is recorded and the letter is delivered. Immediately request your guild to recommend one person familiar with goods within three days of receiving this letter and report to this chamber to jointly organize a commercial inspection committee for Japanese goods, which is extremely important. Do not delay.

News from the Executive Committee of the Anti-Japanese Association

The Anti-Japanese Aid Overseas Chinese Committee held its third executive committee meeting at 5 p.m. yesterday, resolving concrete measures for resisting Japanese goods. Details are recorded as follows:

▲ Concrete Measures for Resisting Goods. During the third executive committee meeting, the proposal for concrete plans to resist Japanese goods, submitted by committee member Chen Songyuan, was discussed in detail by those present. It was resolved that the principles are as follows: All Japanese goods should be permanently resisted. However, for essential industrial raw materials, if there are currently no other goods that can replace them, each factory should provide a detailed list of the names and quantities of the required Japanese goods and report to the association. Those already determined should immediately come to the association to register, and those to be determined should first come to the association to apply. After that, a time limit will be set, and each industry guild should raise funds to establish factories and manufacture them themselves in order to gradually reduce them year by year. As for other items, Tao Baichuan, Yu Hualong, Zhu Yingpeng, Li Wenjie, and Fang Jiaobo, five committee members, were assigned to review them.

▲ Resolutions of the Executive Committee. The following cases were also discussed and resolved: (1) Organization of the Custody Committee: Resolved: No discussion, maintain the original plan. (2) Request from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, etc., to release the detained Japanese goods: Resolved: The request will only be reserved until the association decides on a method for disposing of the detained Japanese goods. (3) Proposal from the Standing Committee to ratify the confiscation of 30 pieces of smuggled and seized Japanese goods: Resolved: Approved for ratification. (7) A letter from Kaicheng Acid Manufacturing Company requesting to order machines and immediately release them, and whether the investigation department's investigation confirms that they can be released: Resolved: Approved for release. (8) The association's relief to overseas Chinese should be actively carried out: Resolved: Send a letter to the Economic Committee for verification. (9) Submit a petition to the National Government regarding the Wanbaoshan incident for serious negotiations: Resolved: Passed.

(2) This time, the boycott of Japanese goods must be thoroughly investigated. (3) Implementation steps and discipline: (A) Submit a letter to the Anti-Japanese Support Association for filing. (C) Jointly form an inspection team with the Transportation and Customs Brokerage Guild to avoid abuses. (D) If any members undermine the patriotic movement, request the higher authorities to expel them from membership and permanently exclude them from serving in the customs brokerage industry. (E) Issue a letter to all members.

▲ Ban Japanese Merchants from Customs Declaration. This great catastrophe is unprecedented. The Japanese conspiracy is as poisonous as a viper. We deeply admire their loyalty and righteousness. The union has already resolved at the general meeting on the 26th to follow the association and unanimously engage in anti-Japanese work. Therefore, we specially send this letter to the association for filing in order to unify efforts. Furthermore, we request that the higher authorities submit on our behalf and forward to the central government, please the National Government to order the Executive Yuan to instruct the Ministry of Finance to send a telegram to the customs of all provinces and cities, strictly prohibiting Japanese merchants from directly declaring and exporting to customs in order to avoid leaks and save national rights.

▲ Changshu Sends a Telegram in Response. Upon hearing this, who would not be moved? Japan has always regarded our country as the target of its economic invasion. If we can rigorously implement severance, it will be enough to control its fate. Shanghai is the largest commercial center in the country. In addition to sending telegrams to various counties for unanimous implementation, we specially send this telegram to express our encouragement. Changshu County Anti-Japanese Aid Overseas Chinese Congress, Chairman Shen Zuguang, and others signed.

▲ County Anti-Japanese Association Established Yesterday

All sectors of Shanghai County held an Anti-Japanese Aid Overseas Chinese Congress at Beiqiao at 10 a.m. yesterday. (3) Submit a petition to the central government to sever diplomatic relations with Japan. Resolved: Passed. (4) Submit a petition to the central government to punish Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting. Resolved: Passed.

▲ Advocates for Severing Diplomatic Relations with Japan. The association submitted a petition to the central government yesterday, stating: A petition for declaring the severance of diplomatic relations with Japan. The Wanbaoshan incident originated from a very minor cause, but the Japanese used it to expand the dispute, incite anti-Chinese sentiment, alienate the feelings between the Chinese and Korean nations, and destroy the foundation of the Chinese people's commerce in Korea, so as to take advantage of the fire, engulf the property of overseas Chinese merchants, and actively invade with the Manchuria-Mongolia policy. Failing to immediately destroy our Eastern Provinces, they devised a way to massacre and expel the overseas Chinese, and transplant Korean residents into our territory, so that the entire Korean Peninsula would be owned by them, in order to accommodate their surplus population and resolve their domestic panic. Their intentions are sinister, and their plans are vicious. Since the establishment of diplomatic relations between China and Japan, they first invaded Ryukyu, then occupied Korea, finally ceded Taiwan, and then seized Jiaozhou, strongly occupying the Korean Peninsula. The shame of the Twenty-One Demands has not been erased, and the brutality of the May 30th Massacre has reappeared. The establishment of the South Manchuria Railway Company is treating us with the strategy of England destroying India. The mainland of China is gradually being eaten away. If we do not take a decisive attitude and sever relations with them, the Japanese will take an inch and want a mile. What future can we expect? The entire population of the county's Anti-Japanese Aid Overseas Chinese Congress unanimously resolved to submit a petition to the central government to promptly maintain diplomacy, elaborate on measures, and declare the severance of diplomatic relations with Japan. All Chinese and Japanese overseas residents should return to their respective countries, and all assets in their locations should be confiscated. If the Japanese use this as an excuse to provoke trouble, the people of the country will swear to rise up armed and be the country's backing. Even if we resort to the final solution, we will not hesitate.

As the saying goes, "It is better to have one frank scholar than a thousand yes-men." I hope you will understand this and respectfully present this telegram. I pray for your consideration. Yu Qiaqing respectfully bows.

Details of Disaster Relief in Jiangxi

▲ Relief Methods Divided into Emergency Relief, Work Relief, and Agricultural Relief

▲ Procedures for Each Type Divided into Three Phases

The Shanghai Fundraising Association for Emergency Relief in Jiangxi received a telegram yesterday from disaster investigators Wei Ruifeng and Wu Jiasan, detailing the disaster relief methods in Jiangxi. The original telegram is recorded below: (Above omitted) I don't know if you have replied to the two telegrams sent earlier. Commander Xiong is very concerned. Disaster relief measures have been determined in Jiangxi. The details are as follows: Emergency relief measures, three phases: Phase 1: Refugees are received by emergency relief centers established in each county. Phase 2: Refugees are sent back to their original homes and assigned to road work. Phase 3: Disabled refugees are accommodated after the end of the accommodation period and resettled separately by each county. Work relief is also divided into three phases: Phase 1: Establish a work relief road construction acceptance office, determine the road construction route, determine the location of the segmented start of construction, and notify the road workers of the assembly point. Phase 2: Direct and designate the road workers' assembly point, send the refugees who are working to start work, and distribute relief according to their names. Phase 3: Complete the planned route and end the work relief. Agricultural affairs are also divided into three phases, regarding farmers' bank matters: Phase 1: Establish a preparatory office and announce various regulations. Phase 2: The head office begins operations, prepares for the establishment of county offices, and begins lending to credit cooperatives. Regarding rural cooperatives: Phase 1: Announce various cooperative regulations, forms, books, and prepare guidance personnel. Phase 2: Establish credit cooperatives in various villages, and promote agricultural cooperatives, consumer cooperatives, and transportation cooperatives in various villages. Phase 3: Credit cooperatives begin lending, and other types of cooperatives are successively established. The Rural Revitalization Committee: Phase 1: Handle the fields scattered by the bandits, register and investigate the households in each village. Phase 2: Handle the allocation of land based on the number of people, guide the villages, establish credit cooperatives, investigate property rights, and handle land surveys. Phase 3: Determine highway property rights, sort out the boundaries of public and private fields, handle land registration, and urge the establishment of various cooperatives. Secretary Wei Keqiang, Advisor Wu Jiasan.

Local News Two

Record of Interrogation of Kidnappers in the Ye Zengshou Case

▲Ye himself unwilling to appear in court

▲Xu and Chen detained for further interrogation

Ye Zengshou, the owner of Zhongfu Import and Export Company, was kidnapped on the morning of the 4th of this month while traveling by his private car No. 4529 with his third concubine, Ms. Fan, from Yulin Road, Yangshupu, to North Sichuan Road for eye treatment. After ten days, he was finally rescued and returned safely. The Public Concession Police have now arrested two kidnappers and one suspect in connection with the case. The following is a description of the events from Ye's kidnapping to the capture of the kidnappers and the court interrogation:

▲The Kidnapping Circumstances: On the morning of July 4th at 10:00 AM, Ye, accompanied by his third concubine, departed from their residence in car No. 4529 and instructed the driver to proceed to a certain ophthalmologist's clinic on North Sichuan Road for treatment. However, as the car proceeded along Yulin Road, its speed suddenly slowed down at a corner. At that moment, three kidnappers jumped onto the car from the roadside. One kidnapper, holding a handgun, sat next to Ye, while the other two sat next to the driver. Ye and the others did not dare to make a sound, and the car came to a halt. Subsequently, the kidnapper sitting at the front of the car manipulated the engine, and the car sped away, disappearing without a trace.

▲Police Witness: At that time, Li Yingbao, the police officer No. 1563 of the Guangde Pawnshop at No. 18 Yulin Road, witnessed the kidnappers' actions. However, as neither the kidnapped person nor his driver showed any signs of seeking help or resistance, he did not suspect a kidnapping. According to the officer's statement, if he had known it was a kidnapping at the time, he could have easily shot them, and Ye would not have been kidnapped.

▲Location of Captivity: On the same day, after succeeding in their plan, the kidnappers drove the car to Xiangyin Road in Jiangwan, abandoned Ye's concubine and took Ye into a bungalow at No. 26, where they confined him. Three kidnappers were assigned to guard him in shifts, never leaving his side. They then sent a letter to Ye's family, demanding 10,000 yuan for ransom. It was not until the 13th, when the kidnappers obtained the money, that they released Ye.

▲Arrest of Three Individuals: Recently, Wang Xichang, a detective of the Public Concession Police, learned that Xu A'gen and Xu Rongfu, both from Ningbo, were hiding at No. 160 North Shanxi Road and were kidnappers. He secretly arrested them all together. Upon investigation, it was discovered that A'gen was indeed one of the kidnappers of Ye, while Rongfu appeared to be unrelated. A'gen also confessed that the bungalow where Ye was held captive was rented by Chen Xingjiang, a local resident living at No. 32 Xiangyin Road. Therefore, Chen was subsequently arrested the day before yesterday.

▲Principal Absent: Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the Special District Local Court, where Judge Ge Zhitan held a trial. However, Ye Zengshou did not appear in court. According to Wang Yaotang, the police lawyer, the police had sent for Ye, but his family claimed that Ye was still in Hangzhou and had not returned. The police, needing to understand everything, specifically sent a letter to the Hangzhou Public Security Bureau, requesting Ye to return to the bureau promptly. However, the bureau replied that Ye had already come to Shanghai and they did not know why he was unwilling to appear in court. However, according to the confessions of the defendants obtained by the police, there were many inconsistencies with the reports from the victim's family. Therefore, it was necessary for Ye to appear in court to clarify the case. Currently, aside from Xu Rongfu, who was found to be unrelated and should be released immediately, the remaining two individuals should be prosecuted under the law for punishing kidnappers, and the hearing should be postponed to allow Ye to appear in court for further questioning.

▲Negotiations by Uncle: Subsequently, Chinese and Western detectives reported the arrest of the defendants and the investigation process. When questioned, Xu A'gen confessed, "I was not present during the kidnapping. Later, an uncle (娘舅) called me to see the hostage. I took a public bus from the North Station to Chen Xingjiang's house first, then went to the bungalow at No. 26. Besides me, there were also A'mao, Zhang Da, Gui Bao, etc. We stayed for about eight or nine days. On the morning of the 13th at 9:00 AM, I went home, so I was not present when Ye was ransomed. I heard the ransom was 10,000 yuan, negotiated by the uncle with the other party. On the 14th, I went to the Zhongnan Restaurant in Dapuqiao, and the uncle gave me banknotes, saying it was 100 yuan, but when I counted it at home, it was only 75 yuan. Our leader's name is San Rongfu." He was arrested for asking for debt at my house, he had nothing to do with this case.

▲Renting Process: Chen Xingjiang confessed, "I met the uncle when I worked at Gaochang Temple, but I don't really know his real name. On July 2nd, he suddenly came to my house to rent the spare room, saying he would only live for three or four days, so I rented him the bungalow. On the 4th, I saw three people entering the house, but I didn't see the hostage. The door was closed all day. They lived for about eight or nine days before terminating the lease. He originally promised to pay 160 yuan for rent, but when I asked for it, he refused to pay. Therefore, I had an argument with the people in the house. Finally, the uncle mediated and gave me 20 yuan." Judge Ge, having obtained the confessions, stated that since Xu Rongfu had been verified to be innocent, he should be released immediately, and the other two defendants should be remanded in custody for a further hearing at a later date.

Lawyer Tan Yigong Liquidates Huang Chujiu's Assets

Legal Opinion

Submitting a draft legal opinion on the liquidation of Huang Chujiu's estate and debts, requesting prompt approval and implementation. The late Huang Chujiu, during his lifetime, engaged in business and accumulated significant debts. He worked hard throughout his life and died in sorrow and indignation. His family members, upholding his will, willingly compiled a catalog of all his estate and submitted it to your office for declaration of liquidation. Fortunately, it has been approved, so Huang's wish has been fulfilled. Although creditors of the Gongfa Company may have suspected the Huang family of concealing assets, nothing has been found to date. This should clear Huang of any wrongs and shows the extent of his financial ruin. However, considering that many of the Gongfa Company creditors are poor families who have been running around and appealing for half a year, eagerly awaiting payment, and have only received 10% of what they are owed, their situation is also pitiable. Huang Chujiu was the largest debtor of Gongfa Company. If Huang's estate can be sold off early to repay debts, then the creditors of Gongfa Company will indirectly benefit from it. This lawyer, entrusted by Huang's family to take on the task of liquidating the estate, dares not forget to protect Huang's legitimate rights. However, whenever I think of the plight of the Gongfa Company creditors, I would rather advise Huang's family to make as much sacrifice as possible. Therefore, since your office approved the declaration of liquidation, I have allowed the liquidators Wu and Pan, two accountants representing the interests of Gongfa Company, to preside over the affairs, hoping to be impartial and quickly resolve the situation, so as to reduce the losses of both creditors and debtors. Unexpectedly, the accountants believe they have gained the trust of your office and have lawyers representing some of the Gongfa Company creditors as their backing, and can act arbitrarily without any scruples. They do not allow Huang's liquidators to be informed beforehand and force them to agree afterwards. They disregard Huang's due rights and other debts owed by Huang personally, not caring for them at all. The lawyers representing some of the Gongfa Company creditors are attacking and seizing Huang's legitimate interests on various pretexts, relying on their ability to use the cries of the majority of ignorant creditors as a means to intimidate Huang's family. The accountants are also using Huang Xianzong's unfounded criminal case as a tool to control Huang's family. As a result, there is a lot of shady dealing and fairness is not being upheld. This lawyer, entrusted with the liquidation, has personally witnessed and cannot remain silent. After investigating the causes, it is due to the fact that the following legal relationships have not been clarified. I will now explain them separately:

(1) Legal points regarding the submission of Huang Chujiu's entire estate for safekeeping by the court: Submitting a catalog of all the assets left by Huang Chujiu to your office in preparation for selling them off and distributing them to repay all debts is fulfilling the debtor's responsibility. Your office appointing the accountants Wu and Pan to take over the movable property first and jointly discuss methods for the immovable property is a protective measure taken to maintain the interests of Huang's creditors, and serves to supervise the liquidation. It should not be the case that once the catalog of assets is submitted to the court, it is deemed that the Gongfa Company creditors have obtained ownership of the assets and can freely claim and dispose of them, leaving Huang in a position of no rights. If this submission is agreed to by all of Huang's creditors, who petition the court to treat all the submitted assets as full settlement of all debts and are willing to exempt Huang's debtors from future responsibilities, and is approved by the court, and all lawsuits regarding Huang's debts in various courts are withdrawn, then Huang's family can declare the liquidation completed and not interfere with the disposal of the submitted assets and the debt distribution methods. Otherwise, how can Huang's reasonable claims be rejected?

(2) Legal points regarding the approval of the declaration of liquidation: As China's bankruptcy law has not yet been implemented, according to the practice of your office, a request to declare the liquidation of all debts with all the debtor's assets is a quasi-bankruptcy procedure, which is legally valid. The judgment of your office approving Huang's declaration of liquidation states that Huang Xianyao and Xianzhong petitioned for the declaration of liquidation and approval to use all the assets left by their late father to pay off all his private and business debts (omitted). This is a legal recognition of quasi-bankruptcy. The subsequent instructions on which items should be sold and which should be retained, tasking the accountants to discuss methods with Huang's agents and report them for approval, clearly state that Huang's family is not allowed to be exempted from the debtor's responsibility for liquidation. Since Huang's family is not exempted from the responsibility of liquidation, all asset sales and debt repayments fall within the authority of Huang's liquidators and cannot be bypassed. The accountants, appointed by your office to discuss the methods together, are in a position of supervision and assistance and are clearly not granted the power to liquidate independently. If Huang's liquidation behavior is found to be inappropriate or to harm the interests of Huang's creditors, the supervisors have the right to express objections and can instruct on methods. If Huang's liquidators do not comply with the instructions, they can petition the court for a ruling. If Huang, the debtor, is not exempted from the responsibility of liquidation but is not granted the power of liquidation, how can Huang act?

(3) Legal points regarding the Gongfa Company liquidator's sole disposal of Huang Chujiu's estate: Since no one is responsible for the liquidation of Gongfa Company, your office has appointed someone to act on behalf of the liquidation of Huang Chujiu's estate and debts. Since his family has entrusted a lawyer to handle the liquidation, the court does not need to appoint another liquidator. This is similar to the case where a criminal defendant has selected a lawyer for defense, and the court does not appoint a separate defense counsel, or a civil defendant has entrusted a lawyer as an agent, and the court does not appoint a special agent. Gongfa Company, in relation to Huang's family, is in the position of a partial creditor. It is perfectly reasonable for the Gongfa Company's liquidator to claim debts from Huang's family, but it is even more baseless for them to directly carry out the liquidation affairs and solely dispose of Huang's entire estate. (To be continued)

Tragic Accident of a Child Jumping off a Train and Having His Arm Crushed

▲Life may be spared

▲Disability may be unavoidable

Zhu Changfu, a blacksmith from the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway Main Machinery Factory in Songnan, is from Wuxi and currently resides at No. 62 Hefeng Road, Wusong. Changfu returned to his hometown on his day off the day before yesterday. His son, Zhenggen, aged eleven, went to the train station to meet his father around 5:00 PM the day before yesterday because his father had not returned. When the train arrived at Wusong, he still did not see his father, so he boarded the train, planning to go to Fort Taiwan to play. As the train entered the station, it had not yet come to a complete stop, and he jumped off. Unexpectedly, he lost his footing and fell onto the tracks. His left arm was crushed by the train wheels, and four fingers on his right hand were also severed. He was rescued and passed out due to the extreme pain, falling to the ground, covered in blood and flesh, unconscious. The stationmaster, unable to find his family, ordered someone to carry him onto the original train and send him to the Shanghai Railway Hospital for treatment. It was not until yesterday morning that his father returned to Wusong and was informed of the situation. Changfu went to investigate and rushed to the hospital. At that time, the doctor had just given him anesthesia to perform surgery. Changfu confirmed that it was his son, but the tragic sight was unbearable to witness. According to the doctor, the child was seriously injured, and there was no certainty at the moment. Life may be spared, but disability is unavoidable. It is noted that in the Wusong train station area recently, there have often been groups of children around the age of ten jumping on and off trains around 5:00 PM, playing around. Parents must prohibit this, otherwise, someone like Zhu Zhenggen can serve as a warning.

Development of the Chinese Harmonica Association

▲Holding a Harmonica Tea Dance Party

▲Continuing to recruit new male and female members

The Chinese Harmonica Association, organized by harmonica master Mr. Wang Qingxun, although it has not been a year since its establishment last year, has been exceptionally earnest and taught effectively by Mr. Wang. Therefore, the members of each session, regardless of gender, age, can learn all kinds of the newest harmonica playing methods within one or two months, such as single note, tremolo, arpeggio, accent, vibrato, grace notes, third and fifth chords, high and low semitones, etc., and can freely play famous Chinese and Western popular songs. The membership fee is only three or four yuan per person, including lecture notes and music scores. Members receive half-price or free preferential treatment for concerts, tea parties, etc. Therefore, the number of members has reached 560. Even people from remote places such as Sichuan, Yunnan, and Nanyang have flocked here. There are former Qing scholars, boudoir celebrities, and people from industrial, commercial, and academic circles, which shows the enthusiasm and interest of the general public in harmonica music. The association holds a social gathering every quarter as usual to connect members' feelings and promote high-end entertainment. It is heard that the association has scheduled for August 2nd (Sunday) at 4:00 PM at the Astor House Hotel outside the Waibaidu Bridge to hold the first "Harmonica Tea Dance Party" for all members. In addition to inviting the association's sponsors Lin Kanghou, Cai Yuanpei, Chen Tingrui, and other celebrities to give speeches or perform, there will also be music and games to add to the fun. The August "Elementary Harmonica Class" and "Special Class" continue to recruit. Those who are interested in studying the harmonica can go to the association's office on the third floor of No. 168 Sichuan Road at the intersection of Beijing Road to obtain detailed information.

Wang Zhongshi Dies of Acute Plague

Wang Zhongshi, a man from Yangzhou, aged twenty-nine, who ran a small book stall at the entrance of Meiyuan Road, Haichang Road, Zhabei, suddenly suffered from an acute plague yesterday and died next to the book stall without anyone to rescue him. He only had a father at home, who was smoking opium and was in the Caohejing Prison for official business. Besides this, there were no other relatives, so no one collected the body. Therefore, the eleventh district head Shen Xiaohe reported to the local court for inspection. Prosecutor Wu and others went to the scene and confirmed that he had died of the plague. They instructed the charity to collect the body and wait for the family to claim it.

Ciyou Association Thanks the Railway Bureau

▲Decides to hold a memorial for Song's mother

The Chinese Ciyou Association received a letter from the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration yesterday stating, "We are writing to inform you that the notice from the funeral committee of the late Madam Song states that if people would like to give condolence gifts, they should donate directly to various charitable and public welfare organizations and submit the receipts to this office for entry into the registry. This bureau now intends to donate twenty yuan for the late Madam Song's condolences to your association for assistance with expenses. We enclose twenty yuan in cash and a letter for your reference. Please issue a receipt for delivery to the Song residence. Sincerely, the Chinese Ciyou Association on the fifth floor of No. 20 Bowuyuan Road in this city." The association decided to hold a memorial for the late Madam Song with the money received from the condolence gifts to commemorate her forever, so as not to betray the late Madam Song's enthusiasm for charity.

The Case of Zhong Hangsu's Wife Requesting Cohabitation is Being Attempted to be Reconciled

Zhong Wang Lifu, a woman from Jiangxi, recently hired lawyers Xue Jiaqi and Wang Zuxun to file a lawsuit in the local court against her husband, Zhong Hangsu (also known as Zhong Wuchang, a professor at Fudan University in Jiangwan), for malicious abandonment and violation of the duty of mutual assistance between husband and wife, requesting a judgment ordering cohabitation. Yesterday morning, Judge Tong Shenglv specially opened the eighth courtroom to hear the case. According to the plaintiff Zhong Wang Lifu, she is thirty-six years old, from Jiangxi, and lives in Mingde Lane, Malang Road. Her husband, Zhong Hangsu, is a teacher at Fudan University. I came to Shanghai in the early October of last year. We got married in the fifth year of the Republic (1916). I came to Shanghai in the seventh year (1918) and returned to my hometown in the seventeenth year (1928) to visit my parents. In the eighteenth year (1929), due to the rampant Communist bandits in Jiangxi Province, I took refuge in Nanchang. In the nineteenth year (1930) in April, I took refuge in Sha with my mother and brother. I wrote to the defendant many times, but there was still no news. In September, I went to the defendant's sixth brother's place in Suzhou. According to the brother-in-law, the defendant had decided to divorce the plaintiff and had proposed five conditions: (1) Forever terminate the common life, (2) Give me two hundred yuan and let me return to my hometown in Jiangxi, (3) Give me four hundred yuan for living expenses every year, (4) Either return to Sichuan or return to Jiangxi, as I wish (Zhong claims to be from Sichuan), (5) (The man marries the woman's family, and each does not interfere with the other. These conditions are actually a disguised divorce. However, my eldest son, who is already thirteen years old this year, my second daughter, who is eight years old, and my youngest son, who is six years old, demand to complete cohabitation." Secondly, according to the defendant Zhong Hangsu, he is thirty-six years old and from Fucheng County, Sichuan. All the evidence is with lawyer Shan Yuhua, and he requests an extension. The plaintiff is indeed my wife, and there is no question about the marriage. I also do not oppose cohabitation. The judge asked, "The defendant is also willing to cohabit, so let's try reconciliation." He also told the defendant, "Husbands and wives should not hurt feelings, especially since you have received higher education. Moreover, the plaintiff has already given birth to three children." The defendant said, "I insist on ordering the plaintiff to return to my home in Sichuan." The judge said, "The road to Sichuan is difficult. Husbands and wives should follow each other closely. Since you work in Shanghai, your wife should also cohabit with you in Shanghai." The defendant replied, "I won't work at Fudan University anymore." The judge said, "This court cannot interfere with so much." He also told both parties to schedule a continued hearing on the 31st of this month and instructed both parties to try reconciliation outside the court. The court was adjourned.

The Municipal Government Revises the Regulations of the Autonomous Training Institute

The Shanghai Municipal Government, recently referring to the regulations approved by the Ministry of Interior, drafted twenty-seven articles of the Shanghai Municipal Local Autonomous Training Institute Regulations, submitted them to the 186th Municipal Conference for deliberation and approval, and they have been officially announced. The text of the articles is recorded as follows:

▲Regulations of the Shanghai Municipal Local Autonomous Training Institute

Chapter 1: General Principles, Article 1: This institute, referring to the regulations of the Autonomous Training Institute of the Ministry of Interior, trains local autonomous talents for Shanghai Municipality. Article 2: This institute is directly under the Shanghai Municipal Government. Chapter 2: Organization, Article 3: This institute shall have one director, concurrently held by the mayor; one deputy director, appointed by the mayor. Article 4: This institute shall have three sections: academic affairs, student affairs, and general affairs. Each section shall have one director and one to three staff members, appointed by the director. Article 5: The teachers of this institute shall be employed by the director. Directors and staff members may also serve as teachers, but the courses they teach shall not interfere with their duties. Article 6: This institute may employ employees, the number of whom shall be determined by the director according to the complexity of the affairs. Chapter 3: Responsibilities, Article 7: The director presides over all affairs of this institute, and the deputy director assists the director in managing all institute affairs. Article 8: The academic affairs section is responsible for compiling courses, reviewing teaching materials, registering student records, organizing grades, and other academic matters. Article 9: The student affairs section is responsible for rectifying student discipline, guiding student life, examining student conduct, auditing student attendance, training student physical fitness, and other student affairs matters. Article 10: The general affairs section is responsible for drafting documents, receiving and dispatching documents, safeguarding seals, preparing budgets and final accounts, handling general affairs accounting, and affairs not belonging to other sections. Article 11: The directors of each section, under the direction of the director and deputy director, are in charge of the affairs of their respective sections. Staff members, in consultation with the director, handle the affairs of each section separately. Article 12: Employees, under the command of senior staff, handle writing, mimeographing, and other matters. Chapter 4: Enrollment, Article 13: Students of this institute shall be recommended by various municipal agencies of this city, but must pass the examination before being admitted. The number of recommendations shall be determined by the mayor. Article 14: Any citizen of the Republic of China, aged twenty-five or above, who meets one of the following qualifications may be recommended by various municipal agencies of this city to take the entrance examination: 1. A member of the Chinese Nationalist Party. 2. A graduate of a junior high school or a school equivalent to a junior high school. 3. Has worked in an administrative capacity for more than one year in an agency under the jurisdiction of the National Government. 4. Has experience in running local public welfare affairs. The qualifications in the first to third clauses of the preceding paragraph must be verified with documents. The qualification in the fourth clause must be guaranteed by the head of the original recommending agency. Article 15: Those who have one of the following circumstances shall not be allowed to take the entrance examination. If the school discovers after admission, their studies may be cancelled at any time: 1. Has engaged in counter-revolutionary activities and has been convicted. 2. Corrupt officials, corrupt clerks, local tyrants, and evil gentry who have been convicted. 3. Expelled from the Chinese Nationalist Party or punished by banning... those who have recovered... those who... those who are incompetent... those who are mentally deranged and physically weak. Article 16: The entrance examination shall be divided into two types: written and oral. The written examination shall consist of: 1. Chinese language, 2. General knowledge. The oral examination shall consist of: 1. Psychological test, 2. Intelligence test. All candidates must first undergo a physical examination and may only take the examination after passing the examination. Chapter 5: Curriculum, Article 17: The curriculum of this institute is as follows: 1. The Three Principles of the People, 2. The Fundamentals of National Reconstruction, 3. The Outline of National Reconstruction, 4. The Provisional Constitution of the Republic of China, 5. The Organic Law of the National Government, with the Organic Law of the Municipality, 6. Civil Law, 7. Household Registration Law, 8. Association Law, 9. Local Autonomy, 10. General Introduction to Economics and Finance, 11. Rural and Land Economics, 12. Business Management Law, 13. Essentials of Health Administration, 14. Statistics, 15. Bookkeeping, 16. Geography, 17. Cooperative Theory, 18. Essentials of Surveying and Practical Training, 19. Official Document Format and Applied Writing, 20. Military Training. Chapter 6: Graduation, Article 18: The training period of this institute shall be two years, but it may be shortened if deemed necessary. Article 19: Upon completion of the training period, the director shall hold a graduation examination on a regular basis. Article 20: Those who fail the graduation examination may be required to take remedial classes within a specified period. If they fail again, they shall be ordered to withdraw from school. Article 21: Graduates of the school will be issued certificates by this institute. Article 22: The institute will prepare a list of graduates and send it to the municipal government for submission to the Ministry of Interior for record. Article 23: After graduation, students will obtain the qualifications in Article 46, Paragraph 1, Item 5, Article 56, Item 2, Article 89, Paragraph 1, Item 5 of the Municipal Organization Law, Article 6, Paragraph 1, Item 5, Article 43, Item 2 of the District Autonomy Implementation Law, and Article 11, Paragraph 1, Item 5 of the Township Autonomy Implementation Law. Chapter 7: Supplementary Provisions, Article 24: During the training period, in addition to collecting food and lodging and uniform fees, all necessary books and lectures will be provided by the institute. Article 25: Various rules of this institute shall be determined separately. Article 26: If there are any matters not covered in these regulations, they may be amended at any time. Article 27: These regulations shall be implemented from the date of promulgation by the Municipal Government.

Exemption of Business Tax for Egg Merchants in Anhui Province

▲Has Been Approved by Ministerial Order

The Shanghai Egg Trade Association, regarding the case of exempting various egg merchants from business tax, earlier presented it to the Shanghai Municipal Association Tax Regulations Research Committee, which was approved by the Ministry of Finance. All egg merchants in the interior are only buying and not selling, without any business income, and should be uniformly exempted in accordance with the ministerial order to ensure fairness. Fearing that the local areas have not received the notification and may cause disturbances, the association again presented it to the Ministry of Finance, requesting the issuance of a notification to the collection agencies of various provinces and cities to follow the ministerial order. Subsequently, a reply was received stating that the Anhui Finance Department had been instructed to comply with the established plan. Because the association found that Anhui Province still had the situation of collecting business tax from egg merchants, which was obviously in conflict with the ministerial order, it sent another telegram to the Ministry of Finance requesting a change to stop it. Yesterday, it received No. 6702 of the Finance Ministry's tax letter, with a telegram stating: "To the Shanghai Egg Trade Association: The Ministry previously received the association's telegram stating that the Anhui Provincial Business Tax Collection Office still collects business tax from egg merchants who set up businesses to collect eggs at the business tax rate. Please change the order to stop it. The Ministry has already ordered the Anhui Finance Department to comply with the established plan and notified the association of the telegram. Now, according to the department's reply, it has already complied with the plan and notified all subordinate collection agencies to comply with it. Please be informed, Finance Ministry, with seal, etc." The association has already notified all members.

Dissent on the Shandong Wharf Surcharge

▲Advocating Not to Establish Separate Items

▲Please the Authorities to Withdraw the Order

Regarding the dispute between Shandong merchants and the local cotton cloth industry over the wharf surcharge, the Bureau of Social Affairs ordered the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce to investigate the business responsibilities and properly mediate, and formulated two points for handling: (1) The procedures for paying the wharf surcharge may be handled by the Shandong merchants entrusting the cotton cloth industry to handle it on their behalf; (2) The Shandong merchants must be responsible for repaying the cotton cloth industry for the surcharge paid, without any shortage. The Shandong Guild Hall was then ordered to inform the Shandong merchants to comply. Afterwards, when buying cloth from various firms, in addition to paying the unified tax and adding transportation costs, an additional wharf surcharge of one mace and three candareens of silver per single package and two mace and six candareens of silver per double package must be paid to the firms to pay on their behalf. After the Guild Hall notified the Shandong merchants, the representatives of the Shandong merchants stated in a letter that the Shandong merchants and the cotton cloth industry have been trading for decades, and all surcharges and other fees have been included in the price of the goods. One party has no trouble entrusting, and the other party has no labor of collecting on their behalf, killing two birds with one stone, which has become a custom. Even if this surcharge should be the responsibility of the buyer, it has always been included in the price of the goods by the seller. Although there is no distinction between the price of the goods and the surcharge on the surface, there is actually no burden of paying on behalf of the buyer. The decades of peaceful and trouble-free habits between the two parties have been overturned at once, and it must be revealed that each single package is added with a wharf surcharge of one mace and three candareens of silver, and each double package is added with two mace and six candareens of silver. Since it is said to be added separately, it means that there has never been such an item. Since there has never been such an item, how can the habits of decades of trading violate the current laws and regulations, or hinder the good customs of society? Moreover, after the dispute between the two parties occurred, more than 270 of the more than 300 cotton cloth industries in the city admitted that they traded as before. If based on the usual trading habits and referring to the current seller's public opinion, this dispute has been resolved without the need for trouble. However, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce did not investigate the situation in detail and listened only to the unilateral demands of a small number of people in the cotton cloth industry and hastily proposed a solution. It is requested to transfer the situation to the Bureau of Social Affairs and withdraw the order, etc. The Guild Hall has already transferred it on their behalf.

The China National Road Construction Association, in commemoration of its tenth anniversary, will hold a large-scale Road and Municipal Exhibition this fall. Someone went to the association's office at No. 16 Renji Road yesterday to inquire about the recent situation of the exhibition, and the details obtained are recorded as follows. The association is scheduled to open on September 12 and last until October 2, for a total of three weeks, and the National Road and Municipal Conference will be held in the second week, bringing together Chinese and foreign road and municipal experts to propose and promote important road and municipal policies. The venue covers an area of ​​about 70 acres, located between Avenue Petain, Rue Cardinal Mercier, and Avenue Pichon in the French Concession. It is heard that this was donated and lent by the Jiaotong and Guohua Banks. The architecture of the venue adopts the inherent form of our country, and the interior layout integrates Chinese and Western styles, striving for magnificence. In addition to the showrooms of various manufacturers, there is also a recreational hall, with an area that can accommodate thousands of people. All items exhibited at the conference are generally exempt from taxes in China. For foreign countries, in addition to samples, documents, charts, and other commodities, only bank guarantees are required when importing other commodities. Those who are transported back to their original places within one month after the closing of the conference do not need to pay taxes. Only those who exceed the time limit or sell them in China will pay taxes in accordance with the regulations. Resolution of the Disturbance Against the Harsh Treatment of Foreign Merchants by the Coal Oil Industry in Jiangsu and Zhejiang Provinces

▲Mobil Oil and Others Have Agreed to Restore Allowances

▲The Coal Oil Industry in Jiangsu and Zhejiang Provinces Takes the Opportunity to Organize a Guild

The coal oil managers in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, because the three companies of Mobil, Asiatic Petroleum, and Texaco reduced allowances, treated them harshly, and affected their business, convened a conference of colleagues in the two provinces in Shanghai to deal with foreign merchants. After further negotiations, a resolution has been reached. The details are recorded below:

▲Opposition to Allowance Reduction: More than 50 Mobil oil colleagues directly managed by Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces include Shanghai Yuxin, Ningbo Fuliyuan, Nanjing Zhang Xintai, Hangzhou Desheng, etc., more than 40 Asiatic Petroleum colleagues directly managed include Shanghai Baochang, Ningbo Jinhua, Zhakou Xiehe, Suzhou Dacheng, etc., and more than 30 Texaco oil colleagues directly managed include Hangzhou Yifengcheng, Shanghai Xiehexing, Zhenjiang Dehe, etc. Branch management offices are not included. According to past practices, Mobil, Asiatic Petroleum, and Texaco provided allowances to direct managers in three colors, that is, 3%, and to branch managers 4%. Now the three banks decided in a meeting that from August 1st, all allowances for direct managers and branch managers would be changed to one color 8, that is, 1.8%, which is half of the previous amount. The entire industry expressed opposition and demanded the restoration of the original allowances. A general meeting was convened in Shanghai and resolved that if the foreign merchants did not make concessions, they would all stop business to show resistance.

▲Resolution Method: On the 16th of this month, the entire industry elected 23 people, including Wang Suizhi, Zhou Shanqing, Fan Ruifu, Wen Gongxuan, and Ma Yuliang, to negotiate with the three banks of Mobil, etc. The heads of major classes and compradors were appointed to negotiate, expressing acceptance of the requests of various managers, but only after the three banks had consulted and replied. The day before yesterday, Mobil hosted a banquet for all colleagues from Jiangsu and Zhejiang in Shanghai at Xinghualou, expressing that part of the interests of managers in various places could be restored. As for Asiatic Petroleum and Texaco, they both sent letters stating that they would follow Mobil as the standard. As a result, the industry disturbance was resolved. For the sake of jointly dealing with the oppression of foreign merchants and contacting feelings, colleagues from various places specially organized the Jiangsu and Zhejiang Coal Oil Industry Guild, which is now actively preparing, and it is heard that it can be formally established soon.

Resolution of the Price Increase Disturbance in the Book Industry

▲Implemented uniformly from July 1st

▲Increase in Binding Machinery and Labor Wages at the Same Time

The local Chinese and foreign bookbinding colleagues, because the workers demanded improved treatment, the mediation committee resolved to increase wages by 10% from July 1st. They also proposed to the Book Industry Association to increase prices by 10%. It has been several months since then, and it has not been resolved. The Bureau of Social Affairs approved the method yesterday and ordered both parties to comply. It is heard that both parties have agreed in order to resolve disputes, and the details are recorded below:

▲Mediation Process: The 22nd was the last mediation date convened by the Bureau of Social Affairs. Xu Hanqing and Lou Weiqing, representatives of the bookbinding industry, Wu Qiuheng, representative of the book industry, Wang Bing and Sheng Yudu, clerks of the Bureau of Social Affairs, attended the meeting. The book industry representatives initially insisted that those above 80 cents for Western binding would not be increased. The bookbinding industry representatives requested that those above 80 cents be increased by 10% and calculated at 80%. After the chairman repeatedly guided them, the book industry representatives agreed to increase the price appropriately, and the bookbinding industry representatives also agreed to reduce the price appropriately. However, because the tasting industry representatives could not fully take responsibility and had to return to the association for instructions, the meeting was adjourned and waited for approval.

▲Approval by the Bureau of Social Affairs: The Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs approved the Shanghai Book Industry Association and the Bookbinding Industry Association yesterday, stating, "Received, the case has been persuaded by the bureau to remove the staff members. Except for the uniform increase of one cent for Chinese binding and one cent for those with six and a half corners for Western binding and five points for those with seven and a half corners, which has been agreed by both representatives, it is now approved to uniformly increase five points for those above eight corners. Please comply with and handle this approval."

▲Agreement by Both Parties: The Bookbinding Industry Association, for the instructions of the Bureau of Social Affairs, has heard that the increase of five points for those above eight corners for Western binding has been expressed to be in compliance. All wages for bookbinding workers will be fulfilled from the date of fulfillment of the increase in the book industry (that is, July 1st). The Book Association, in order to resolve the matter quickly, has also expressed that it can reluctantly agree to the instructions of the Bureau of Social Affairs. After Executive Director Lu Feibohong returns to Shanghai within the next few days, all colleagues will be notified.

A Dead Child in a Mat Package Comes Back to Life

At around 9:00 AM yesterday, Zhuang Shi, a worker from Zhapu Road in Zhabei, collected four corpses of children from various places. Two were placed in wooden boxes, and two were wrapped in broken mats. He carried them to the intersection of Gonghe New Road and Zhongxing Road to rest. The area was right across from the Zhongxing Road Police Station of the Fourth District Public Security Bureau. The guard Li Qingyin suddenly heard crying from the mat package and knew that the dead child had come back to life. He asked the worker, and he learned that the mat package was collected from the lawn in front of Shed C of the Xijin Guild Hall. Officer Li immediately reported to the police chiefs Luo Mingqi, Cheng Jun, and Chen Ruichun, and sent people to investigate the place. It was learned that the family of Sun Bingren, a Siyang native with the house number 17 in Zixingfang, abandoned the child. According to Sun, it was a boy named A Bao, who was two years old. He died at about 2:00 AM yesterday due to ineffective treatment. He had no money to buy a coffin, so he abandoned him there wrapped in a broken mat. The investigators then went with him to open the mat package, and indeed saw that the dead child had come back to life. They couldn't help but be happy from sadness, so they took him home. Onlookers were amazed.

Injury While Playing with a Handgun

The Cai Renmao Glass Shop at No. 139 Tiantong Road, Hongkou, was opened by the owner Cai Renchu. It has been in business for many years and has made a lot of profits. It was coveted by kidnappers. Last year, Cai Renchu was once kidnapped by kidnappers, but fortunately Cai was extremely alert and was not kidnapped. Later, he hired Wang Zuxian, a Tianjin native, as a bodyguard to accompany him in and out, and he was safe and sound. However, Wang shared a room with the old clerk in the shop at night, and they got along well. After 7:00 PM last night, Wang went downstairs to wash his face and casually placed his handgun on the table in the upper room. It was unexpected that the old clerk Li Awu (37 years old, from Changzhou) and Shen Zhongfu (27 years old, from Haimen) happened to see the handgun in the room. Their curiosity arose, and Shen took the gun and played with it at will. He accidentally pulled the trigger, and there was a loud bang. The bullet flew out and hit Li's left back, piercing his right back, and blood flowed like a fountain. Later, someone heard the noise and went upstairs, and sent the injured person to Tongren Hospital for treatment. The hospital reported to the Hongkou Police Station and ordered detectives to come. They took the people involved to the police station for preliminary interrogation and handling.

The boy, named A Bing, was 12 years old. At around 4:00 PM yesterday, while walking along Ouja Road in Hongkou, he was suddenly hit by a No. 2 public bus that was speeding along. He was unable to avoid it in time and was crushed and fell to the ground by the wheels. He was injured in the head and bleeding from the large intestine, and died immediately. After the Shenjiawan Fire Brigade heard the news, they drove a fire truck to Tongren Hospital. An Indigo Boat Suddenly Goes Missing

▲Found at the Datong Wharf

▲The Captain and the Crew Were Detained

At about 9:00 PM the night before yesterday, Xue Silin, a Chinese staff member in the office of the Customs Water Patrol Police Station, reported that the captain of the wharf, Zhang Gui, reported that this morning, 120 boxes and 30 barrels of indigo were transported for the Qianyigong Customs Brokerage on Sima Road and parked at the Sima Road wharf. In the afternoon, he left the boat for some business, leaving the crew Tao Qiusheng and Fan Aguan to guard the boat. When he returned to the boat at 8:00 PM, it was unexpected that the boat, cargo, and crew were completely missing. When he asked the neighboring boat, they said that a small wheel dragged your boat away at 7:30, and I don't know where it went. When I heard the words, I immediately returned to the customs brokerage to report the situation, and then reported to your police station, etc. The Chinese staff member informed the police chief and immediately sent Bao Tans Wu Rongsheng, Ge Changsheng, Sun Agui, Wang Haiquan, and Deng Jiagen, along with armed Chinese police, to take a steam boat to patrol and drive to the Datong Wharf in Nanshi. In the darkness, they saw a small wheel parked there, and the red and green lights on both sides were extinguished. There were shadows on the wheel, about twenty or thirty people. Next to the wheel was a stone wharf boat. The detectives went forward to interrogate and saw seven people holding handguns among the twenty or thirty people. The detectives also took out guns and steel badges for self-defense. Unexpectedly, all those people went ashore and fled without a trace. It was found that the original stolen goods were all on the wharf boat. After checking, only two boxes of indigo were missing. They then took the boat and cargo (the crew had escaped) and the small wheel (named Jiafeng, a wild chicken small wheel of Qiaji Company) and the captain of the small wheel, Ni Heshang, to the police station together. According to the small wheel captain Ni, someone gave him five yuan to hire him to tow the boat, but he didn't know anything else. At about 2:00 AM yesterday morning, Tao Qiusheng and Fan Aguan, two members of the indigo boat, voluntarily surrendered to the police station, claiming that they had left the boat for a long time and had not colluded to steal the original stolen goods, etc. The police chief ordered the two men, along with the small wheel captain, to be detained together, and the small wheel was also temporarily detained. The original stolen goods were taken away by the owner Huang Defeng at 3:00 PM yesterday afternoon, and the fugitives were strictly arrested and brought to justice for investigation.

Radios in Cars

The Eagle King car radio invented by the Greesbeck Radio Factory in Chicago, USA, is used by many people, but it has not been seen in Shanghai yet. Wheeler Company is a giant in the local radio industry, and it covers everything from overseas novel products to the first purchase, so it has long ordered a large number of such radios from the United States. They have now been shipped one after another. It is heard that the machine is not affected by the vibration of the car engine and can avoid the obstruction of the car machine electrical system. The main switch is installed under the steering wheel, directly connected to the radio. There are seven vacuum tubes in the machine, and the power is used from the car's storage battery. There is also a loudspeaker, which is also electromagnetic. The machine can be installed under the front seat floor or in other hidden places, light and compact, economical and durable, loud and unparalleled. It does not cost much to have one in the car, and the fun is endless.
